Nikah — Marriage

Option of a Mukataba Who Bears Her Master's Child
Option for mukataba when she bears child from master

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options available to a mukataba when she bears a child from her master, and explain the legal consequences of each choice.

Core Idea
A mukataba who bears her master's child has the right to choose: complete the kitaba or declare ajz to become an umm walad.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in Hanafi fiqh regarding a female slave who is under a kitaba contract (mukataba) and gives birth to a child from her master. The birth creates a unique legal situation: the child is free (as the master's offspring), and the mother gains the potential status of umm walad. However, she is not automatically freed. Instead, she is given a choice between two paths, each with distinct consequences for her freedom and status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the trigger event
The subject is a mukataba (a female slave who has contracted to purchase her freedom in installments). The trigger event is her giving birth to a child from her master (the owner).
The child is automatically free because the master is the father.
2
State the two options available to her
The text says she has a choice: (1) complete the kitaba by paying the remaining installments and become free, or (2) declare herself incapable (ajz) of paying, which cancels the kitaba and makes her an umm walad (mother of the master's child), with freedom upon the master's death.
The option is hers alone; the master cannot force either path.
3
Analyze the consequence of each option
Option 1: She becomes free immediately after completing payments, with full rights. Option 2: She becomes an umm walad – she cannot be sold, and she becomes free upon the master's death, but meanwhile remains a slave with certain protections.
As umm walad, she is in a transitional status; the child is free from birth.
4
Note the underlying reason for the option
The option exists because childbirth creates a tie to the master (the child is his), and the law grants her a choice to either honor the kitaba or embrace the maternal bond that leads to eventual freedom.
This showcases Hanafi concern for balancing contractual obligations with human relationships.
5
Contrast with a non-mukataba slave
A regular slave who bears a child from her master automatically becomes an umm walad without any option. The mukataba's unique position requires a choice because she already has a path to freedom via the kitaba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مکاتبہ نے آقا سے بچہ جنا تو اسے اختیار ہے چاہے کتابت پوری کرے اور اگر چاہے تو خود کو عاجز کر کے ام ولد ہو جائے
If a mukataba gives birth to a child from the master, then she has the option: if she wishes, she may complete the kitaba, and if she wishes, she may declare herself incapable (ajz) and become an umm walad.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This is a ruling regarding a female mukatab (mukataba) who bears a child from her master. Since the child is the master's, she gains the status of umm walad (mother of the master's child) upon the birth. However, she has not yet been freed. She is given the choice: either continue with the kitaba contract and pay the remaining installments to secure her freedom, or declare herself unable to pay (ajz), which annuls the kitaba and makes her automatically an umm walad. As an umm walad, she becomes free upon the master's death. This option is hers alone.

Key Terms
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who bears a child to her master; she becomes free upon his death.
کتابت (kitaba): A contract between a master and a slave whereby the slave purchases his/her freedom by paying installments.
مکاتبہ (mukataba): A female slave who has entered into a kitaba contract.
عاجز (ajz): Incapability; declaring oneself unable to fulfill the kitaba payments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, what must a mukataba do to become an umm walad after giving birth to her master's child?
A) Nothing; she automatically becomes umm walad.
B) She must complete the kitaba payments.
C) She must declare ajz (inability to pay).
D) She must be sold to another master.

Key Takeaway
A mukataba who bears her master's child has the option to either complete the kitaba and gain freedom, or declare ajz and become an umm walad, with freedom upon the master's death.

Kitabah for a Minor Slave Who Understands Trade
Inter-madhhab dispute on kitabah for a discerning minor slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on kitabah for a discerning minor slave and identify the root cause of the Shafi'i disagreement.

Core Idea
A discerning minor slave can be made a mukatab because his acceptance is valid; the Shafi'i objection rests on a deeper dispute over permission for minors in trade.

In this passage, we encounter a classic inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi school permits making a minor slave a mukatab if he is discerning and understands buying and selling. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, and the disagreement traces back to a fundamental usul issue: whether a discerning child can be given permission to engage in trade. Understanding this dispute illuminates how different schools weigh legal capacity (ahliyyah) and its application in contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: kitabah of a minor slave is permissible (ja'iz) if he is discerning (ya'qil al-bay' wa al-shira').
The reasoning is that such a minor can validly express acceptance, and the contract is beneficial to him.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees; according to him, it is not permissible.
This is an inter-madhhab dispute, not an intra-Hanafi one.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i position is based on the invalidity of idhn al-sabi fi al-tijarah (permission for a minor in trade). They hold that a minor cannot be given valid permission, so his transactions are null.
The passage does not elaborate the Shafi'i dalil beyond this root issue.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the dispute is rooted in the validity of idhn al-sabi fi al-tijarah, which Hanafis affirm. Since they consider the permission valid, the minor's acceptance in kitabah is effective.
The text presents this as a straightforward talil linking the two issues.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis allow kitabah for discerning minors; Shafi'is do not. Additionally, if the minor is not discerning, the contract is void even if someone else pays on his behalf.
This clarifies the boundary condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غلام صغیر کومکا تب بنانے کا حکم
قال وتجوز كتابة العبد الصغير اذا كان يعقل البيع والشراء لتحقق الايجاب والقبول اذ العاقل من اهل القبول والتصرف نافع في حقه والشافعي يخالفنا فيه وهو بناء على مسألة اذن الصبي في التجارة وهذا بخلاف ما اذا كان لا يعقل البيع والشراء لان القبول لا يتحقق منه فلا ينعقد العقد حتى لو ادى عنه غيره لا يعتق ويسترد ما دفع

ترجمہ: اور جائز ہے کہ کم سن غلام کو مکاتب کرنا جب کہ وہ خرید وفروخت کو سمجھتا ہوں۔ ایجاب وقبول متحقق ہونے کی وجہ سے کیونکہ عاقل آدمی اہل قبولیت میں سے ہے اور تصرف اس کے حق میں نافع بھی ہے۔ اور امام شافعی اس میں ہمارے مخالف ہیں اور یہ اختلاف تجارت کے بارے میں اذن صبی کے مسئلہ پر مبنی ہے اور یہ حکم اس کے خلاف ہے جب وہ خرید و فروخت کو نہ سمجھتا ہو۔ کیونکہ اس کی جانب سے قبول متحقق نہیں ہو سکتا۔ نپس عقد منعقد نہ ہوگا۔ حتی کہ اگر اس کی طرف سے کسی غیر نے ادا کر دیا تب بھی آزاد نہ ہوگا اور جو کچھ غیر نے دیا ہے وہ واپس لے لے گا۔

تشريح قوله وتجوز ... الخ: اگر کوئی غلام کم سن ہو اور خرید وفروخت کو سمجھتا ہو کہ شراء جالب ہے اور بیع سالب۔ تو ہمارے یہاں ایسے صغیر غلام کو مکاتب کرنا جائز ہے کیونکہ اس کی جانب سے ایجاب و قبول کا تحقق ہو جائے گا۔ امام شافعی اس میں ہمارے خلاف ہیں ان کے نزدیک عبد صغیر کو مکاتب کرنا جائز نہیں ان کا یہ اختلاف اس اختلافی مسئلہ پر بنی ہے کہ طفل ممیز کو تجارت کی اجازت دینا صحیح ہے یا نہیں؟ سو ہمارے نزدیک صحیح ہے ان کے نزدیک صحیح نہیں۔
Ruling on making a minor slave a mukatab. He (the author) said: The kitabah of a minor slave is permissible if he understands buying and selling, due to the actualization of offer and acceptance, because the intelligent person is among those capable of acceptance, and disposal (tasarruf) is beneficial in his regard. Al-Shafi'i disagrees with us in this, and it is based on the issue of permission for a minor in trade. This is unlike the case where he does not understand buying and selling, because acceptance from him does not actualize, so the contract is not concluded—so much so that even if someone else pays on his behalf, he is not freed and what was paid is taken back. Translation: It is permissible to make a minor slave a mukatab when he understands buying and selling, due to the actualization of offer and acceptance, because an intelligent person is among the people of acceptance, and disposal is beneficial in his right. Imam al-Shafi'i opposes us in this, and this difference is based on the issue of permission for a child (sabi) in trade. This ruling is contrary to when he does not understand buying and selling, because acceptance from him cannot actualize, so the contract will not be concluded. Even if someone else pays on his behalf, he is not freed and what was given is taken back. Commentary on his statement 'and it is permissible...': If a slave is young and understands buying and selling—that buying is attractive and selling is expelling—then according to us, such a minor slave can be made a mukatab because offer and acceptance from him can actualize. Imam al-Shafi'i opposes us in this; according to him, it is not permissible to make a minor slave a mukatab. Their difference is based on the disputed issue of whether permission for a discerning child (tifl mumayyiz) to trade is valid. According to us, it is valid; according to them, it is not.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
Passage type: Inter-madhhab dispute. This section addresses the validity of a kitabah contract with a minor slave. The Hanafi position is clear: if the minor is discerning (mumayyiz) and understands the meaning of buying and selling, then the contract is valid. The reason is that such a minor can validly express acceptance, which is a condition for the contract. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, and the root of the disagreement is a more fundamental usul issue: whether a discerning child can be given permission (idhn) to engage in trade. In the Hanafi school, such permission is valid; thus, the child's actions in trade (and by extension in kitabah) are effective. The Shafi'i school does not recognize the validity of such permission for a minor, so they rule that a minor cannot be a party to kitabah. The passage also notes the consequence if the minor does not understand: the contract is void, and even if someone else pays on his behalf, it does not result in freedom.

Key Terms
عبد صغير (abd saghir): A slave who is a minor (under the age of majority).
مكاتبة (mukatabah): The contract of kitabah, where a slave agrees to pay for his freedom.
اذن الصبي في التجارة (idhn al-sabi fi al-tijarah): Permission granted to a minor to engage in trade; its validity is the underlying issue.
طفل مميز (tifl mumayyiz): A discerning child, one who can understand the implications of transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the underlying issue that causes the disagreement between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding making a minor slave a mukatab?
A) Whether a minor can own property.
B) Whether a discerning child can be given permission to trade.
C) Whether a slave can be freed.
D) Whether offer and acceptance are required.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits kitabah for a discerning minor slave because his acceptance is valid; the Shafi'i objection stems from a deeper disagreement over permission for minors in trade.

Master's Intercourse with Mukatabah: The 'Aqr Obligation
Ruling on 'aqr (dower) when master has intercourse with his mukatabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on 'aqr for a master's intercourse with his mukatabah, compare it with the Maliki and Hanbali views, and explain the evidence based on Quranic analogy.

Core Idea
A master must pay 'aqr for intercourse with his mukatabah because she owns her parts under kitabah.

This lesson examines a specific scenario where a master has intercourse with his female slave who has a kitabah contract. The Hanafi school, along with the Shafi'is, holds that the master must pay a compensation called 'aqr, measured by the dower of a similar free woman. The Maliki and Hanbali positions differ on whether any payment is required. We will explore the proofs and the practical consequences of these differences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling as stated in the text: the master is liable for 'aqr (dower of a similar woman).
2
Identify the opposing views
Note that Imam Malik holds no 'aqr is due, while Imam Ahmad says 'aqr is due only if stipulated; otherwise punishment.
3
Follow the opponents' proofs
Malik argues that ownership permits intercourse without extra payment. Ahmad argues that without stipulation, intercourse is forbidden but not financially compensable.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The mukatabah has become more entitled to her parts than the master due to kitabah; the usufruct of her private part is compensable like a wage, as per Quranic analogy (4:24).
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafi/Shafi'i: master pays 'aqr. Maliki: no payment. Hanbali: payment only if stipulated; otherwise punishment only.
Also note the effect on kitabah if intercourse is stipulated: Hanafi says fasid, Maliki says stipulation fasid but contract valid, Hanbali says both valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله واذا وطى المولى.. الخ - اگر آقا نے اپنی مکاتبہ باندی سے وطی کر لی تو اس کے ذمہ عقر لا زم ہوگا۔ یعنی اسی جیسی عورت کا جو مہر ہوتا ہو وہ دینا پڑے گا۔ امام شافعی بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ امام مالک کے نزدیک عقر واجب نہ ہوگا۔ امام ند فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مکاتبہ سے وطی کرنے کی شرط کر لی ہو تو واجب ہوگا ورنہ نہیں بلکہ سزادی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ یہ ولی حرام ہے۔ بہر کیف حناف و شوافع کے نزدیک وحی شرط کرنے کی صورت میں کتابت فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ امام مالک کے نزدیک شرط فاسد ہوگی اور عقد صحیح ہو جائے گا۔ امام احمد کے نزدیک شرط وعقد دونوں صحیح ہوں گے۔ قوله لا نها صارت اخص .... الخ - وجوب عقر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مکاتبہ مذکورہ آقا کی بہ نسبت اپنے اجزاء کی زیادہ مختار ہو چکی ہے تا کہ اس کے ذریعہ سے کتابت کا مقصود حاصل کیا جائے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ آقا کو مال کتابت حاصل ہو اور اس کے عوض میں باندی کو زادی حاصل ہو۔ اور عورت کے منافع بضعہ چونکہ بمنزلہ اجر اوراعیان ہیں " حيث قابلها الشرع بالا عيان قال الله تعالى وان تبتغوا باموالکم لہذا اسکا استحقاق بھی باندی ہنی کو حاصل ہے۔ پس اس سے منفعت حاصل کرنے میں آقا ضامن ہوگا۔
His statement: 'wa idha wati al-mawla...' - if the master had intercourse with his mukatabah (female slave under kitabah), then he is liable for 'aqr, meaning he must pay the dower of a woman of her status. Imam al-Shafi'i also holds this view. According to Imam Malik, 'aqr is not wajib. Imam Ahmad says that if intercourse was stipulated in the kitabah contract, then 'aqr is wajib, otherwise not; rather, the master should be punished because it is forbidden. In any case, according to Hanafis and Shafi'is, if intercourse is stipulated, the kitabah becomes fasid (defective). According to Malik, only the stipulation becomes fasid, but the contract remains valid. According to Ahmad, both the stipulation and the contract are valid. His statement: 'la annaha sarat akhass...' - the proof for the obligation of 'aqr is that the said mukatabah has become more entitled to her own parts than the master, so that through her the purpose of kitabah is achieved: the master gets the kitabah money and the slave girl gets freedom. The usufruct of her private part is like a wage and an asset, as the Law has compared it to assets (Quran: 'and that you seek [marriage] with your wealth'). Therefore, she is entitled to its compensation, and if the master benefits from it, he is liable.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage covers two issues: (1) the ruling on 'aqr when the master has intercourse with his mukatabah, and (2) the effect of stipulating intercourse in the kitabah contract. The Hanafi position is that 'aqr is wajib because the mukatabah has a right over her own person and earnings through the kitabah contract. The author presents the inter-madhhab dispute: Shafi'i agrees with Hanafis; Malik says no 'aqr; Ahmad says 'aqr is due only if stipulated, otherwise the master should be punished. Regarding stipulation, Hanafis and Shafi'is say it makes kitabah fasid (since it implies she is not free to refuse), while Malik says only the stipulation is invalid, and Ahmad says both are valid. The proof for 'aqr is that the mukatabah has become 'more entitled' (akhass) to her body parts because she needs to use them to earn money for the kitabah. The usufruct of the private part (bida') is considered as wealth, as indicated by the Quranic verse 'And that you seek [marriage] with your wealth' (4:24), so exploiting it without compensation requires payment.

Key Terms
عقر ('aqr): The dower (mahr) that must be paid when a master has intercourse with his female slave who has a right to her own earnings under kitabah.
مکاتبہ (mukātabah): A female slave who has entered into a kitabah contract to earn her freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a master has intercourse with his mukatabah?
A) He must pay 'aqr (dower of a similar woman).
B) No payment is required.
C) He must be punished but no financial liability.
D) The kitabah becomes void automatically.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a master to pay 'aqr for intercourse with his mukatabah because the kitabah contract elevates her right to her own body parts, making their use compensable.

Kitabah on a Specific Item Belonging to Another: Ruling, Disputes, and Details
Fiqh ruling with inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kitabah when the compensation is a specific item owned by a third party, explain the qiyas on sale, and identify the key intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disputes.

Core Idea
Kitabah on another's specific item is invalid in Zahir al-Riwayah because deliverability is a condition in commutative contracts.

This lesson dives into the rules of kitabah when the slave is required to deliver a specific item (ayn) that belongs to someone else. The Hanafi school's relied-upon view deems such a contract invalid, but there are important disputes – both within the school and with other madhahib – that revolve around whether the contract resembles sale (which requires deliverability) or dower (which does not). We will walk through the reasoning, the exceptions for currency, and the effect of the owner's permission or the slave's later acquisition of the item.

Guided Path
1
State the basic scenario
Identify that the master makes kitabah with his slave on a specific item (e.g., a horse or a garment) that is owned by a third party. This is the core case under discussion.
2
Identify the Zahir al-Riwayah ruling and its proof
According to the main Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah), the contract is invalid (fasid). The proof is qiyas on sale: in any rescindable commutative contract (mu'awada), the subject matter must be deliverable. Since the slave cannot deliver what he does not own, the contract fails.
Note the distinction: if the compensation were currency (dirhams/dinars) belonging to another, the contract would be valid because currency does not become determinate in commutative contracts.
3
Contrast with the Nawadir narration (Hasan ibn Ziyad)
Hasan ibn Ziyad narrates that the contract is valid: if the slave later acquires the item and delivers it, he becomes free; if unable, he returns to slavery. This view analogizes the contract to dower (mahr) in marriage, where deliverability is not a condition.
This is a rare (nawadir) transmission and not the relied-upon position.
4
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad agree with the Hanafi invalidity (though their reasoning may differ), while Imam Malik holds the contract valid, requiring the slave to buy the item or pay its value if the owner refuses to sell.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi disputes on permission and acquisition
When the owner of the item permits, there are three views: Muhammad says the contract becomes valid; Abu Hanifa says it remains invalid by analogy to the non-permission case; Abu Yusuf says it is valid but with different delivery obligations. If the slave acquires the item, Abu Hanifa (via Abu Yusuf) says he is not freed unless the master explicitly conditioned freedom on payment; another narration from Abu Yusuf says he is freed regardless.
These disputes reflect the tension between the inherent invalidity of the contract and the possibility of performance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المكاتب
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ اور امام ابوحنیفہ سے حسن نے روایت کی کہ عقد جائز ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر وہ اسکا مالک ہو کر آقا کو دے دے تو آزاد ہو جائے گا اور اگر عاجز ہو جائے تو رقیق کر دیا جائیگا۔ کیونکہ بھی مسمی مال ہے اور سپرد کرنے کی قدرت بھی موہوم ہے تو مہر کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ معاوضہ میں مال عین ہی معقود علیہ ہوتا ہے اور معقود علیہ پر قدرت کا ہونا شرط ہے صحت عقد کے لئے جب کہ عقد قابل فسخ ہو جیسے بیع میں ہوتا ہے۔ بخلاف مہر کے جو نکاح میں ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ نکاح سے جو مقصود ہے اس پر قدرت کا ہونا شرط نہیں تو مہر جو تابع ہے اس پر قدرت بدرجہ اولی شرط نہ ہو گی۔
تشریح قوله على شئ بعينه لغيره .... الخ - لغیرہ لفظ شی سے حال ہے اورشی گونکرہ ہے جوذ والحال نہیں ہوسکتا۔ لیکن یہاں بعینہ صفت کی وجہ سے تخصیص آگئی اس لئے ذوالحال ہونا صحیح ہو گیا۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر آقا نے غلام کو کسی دوسرے شخص کی معین چیز مثلاً گھوڑے، کپڑے یا غلام کے عوض مکاتب کیا۔ تو ہمارے اور امام شافعی واحمد کے نزدیک یہ بھی فاسد ہے۔ کیونکہ غلام دوسرے کی چیز سپرد کرنے سے قاصر ہے۔ امام مالک کے نزدیک جائز ہے اب غلام وہ چیز خرید کر دے دے اور اگر مالک فروخت نہ کرے تو اسکی قیمت دے دے۔ قوله و مراده شي ... الخ - علی شی بعینہ میں لفظ شی سے امام محمد کی مراد ایسی چیز ہے جو معین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتی ہے۔ جیسے کپڑا، یہ گھوڑا ، یہ غلام ، یہ مکان وغیرہ اور اگر چہ وہ چیز متعین نہ ہوتی ہو۔ بان قال کاتبتك على هذه الالف الدراهم حالانکہ وہ ہزار درہم کسی غیر کی ملک ہے تو عقد کتابت جائز ہوگا۔ کیونکہ در اہم و دنانیر گوامانت و غصب میں متعین ہو جاتے ہیں۔ لیکن معاوضات میں متعین نہیں ہوتے ۔ پس عقد کتابت ایسے درا ہم سے متعلق ہو گا۔ جو غلام کے ذمہ قرض ہوں گے۔ امام شافعی و امام احمد کے یہاں اس صورت میں بھی کتابت جائز نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ ان کے یہاں درا ہم ودنا نیر بھی متعین ہوتے ہیں۔
قوله رواه الحسن .. الخ - صورت مسئلہ کی تشریح یہ ہے کہ غیر کی چیز پر مکاتب کرنے میں دو صورتیں ہیں ۔ وہ چیز معین کرنے سے متعین ہوگی جیسے گھوڑا ، غلام وغیرہ یا متعین نہ ہوگی۔ جیسے نقود یعنی در اہم ودنا نیر اول کی پھر دو صورتیں ہیں ۔ مالک اس کو جائز رکھے گایا نہیں۔ اگر جائز نہ رکھا تو پھر دو صورتیں ہیں۔ مکاتب یا تو کسی ذریعہ سے اس کا مالک ہو کر آقا کو سپر دکرے گا یا نہیں۔ یہ کل چار صورتیں ہوئیں ۔ پس اگر وہ چیز معین کرنے سے متعین نہ وہ تو عقد کتابت جائز ہوگا ۔ جیسا کہ سابق قول میں بیان ہو چکا اور اگر متعین ہو جاتی ہو اور مالک اس کی اجازت نہ دے اور مکاتب کسی ذریعہ سے اس کا مالک بھی نہ ہو سکے تو ظاہر الروایہ میں جائز نہ ہوگا۔ اور حسن کی روایت میں جائز ہوگا۔ اب اگر مکا تب اس چیز کی ملکیت حاصل کر کے آقا کو دے دے تو آزاد ہو جائے گا اور اگر وہ نہ دے سکے تو رقیق کر دیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ جو چیز مسمی ہے وہ مال ہے اور سپرد کرنے کی قدرت بھی ( ثبوت ملک کے احتمال پر ) موہوم ہے تو مال غیر سے ہونے والا بدل کتابت عورت کے اس مہر کے مشابہ ہو گیا جو غیر کے مال سے ہو۔ مثلا کسی نے عورت سے غیر کے غلام پر نکاح کیا تو تسمیہ صحیح ہے اب اگر غلام کے مالک نے اجازت نہ دی تو عورت شوہر سے غلام کی قیمت لے گی نہ کہ مہر مثل ولو كانت التسمية فاسدة لرجعت بمهر المثل قـولـه قلنا ان العين ... الخ - ظاہر الروایہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ معاوضات میں مال عین ( بدل کتابت ) معقود علیہ ہوتا ہے اور عقد صحیح

كتاب المكاتب
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳
ہونے کے لئے معقود علیہ پر قدرت کا ہونا شرط ہے۔ جب کہ عقد قابل فسخ ہو ۔ جیسے بیع میں ہوتا ہے۔ سوال پہلے گزر چکا کہ بدل کتابت کا حکم ایسا ہے جیسے بیچ میں شمن کا ہوتا ہے اس بنیاد پر کتابت حالہ جائز ہوئی تھی اور شمن معقود یہ ہوتا ہے نہ کہ معقود علیہ تو اس پر قدرت کا ہون شرط نہیں ہو سکتا۔ جواب بدل کتابت کے لئے حکم ثمن کا ہونا اس وقت ہے جب وہ نقود سے ہو اور ہماری گفتگوشی عین کے بارے میں ہے کہ عین کی صورت میں عقد کتابت بمنزلہ مقابضہ ہو گا اور بدل کتابت کے لئے مبیع کا حکم ہوگا نہ کہ من کا۔
قوله بخلاف الصداق الخ - روایت حسن میں ” فاشبہ الصداق“ کا جواب ہے کہ بخلاف مہر کے جو نکاح میں ہوتا ہے کہ نکاح میں صحت تسمیہ کے لئے مسمی کا صرف قیمتی مال ہونا شرط ہے مقدور التسلیم ہونا شرط نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ نکاح سے جو اصلی مقصود ہے۔ یعنی توالد و تناسل ( اور بقول صاحب نہایہ منافع بضع ) اس پر قدرت کا ہونا شرط نہیں ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ دودھ پیتی بچی سے نکاح جائز ہے۔ ( گو قدرت معدوم ہے ) تو جو چیز مقصود نہیں بلکہ تابع ہے۔ یعنی مہر اس پر قدرت کا ہونا بطریق اولی شرط نہ ہوگا۔
اگر مالک مین نے اس کو جائز رکھا تو پھر جائز ہے یا نہیں
فلو اجاز صاحب العين ذلك فعن محمد انه يجوز لانه يجوز البيع عند الاجازة فالكتابة اولى وعن أبي حنيفة انه لا يجوز اعتبارا بحال عدم الاجازة على ما قال في كتاب والجامع بينهما انه لا يفيد ملك المكاتب وهو المقصود لانها تثبت للحاجة الى الاداء منها ولا حاجة فيما اذا كان البدل عينا معينا والمسألة فيه على ما بينا وعن ابى يوسف انه يجوز اجاز ذلك او لم يجز غير انه عند الاجازة يجب تسليم عينه وعند عدمها يجب تسليم قيمته كما فى النكاح والجامع بينهما صحة التسمية لكونه مالا ولو ملک المكاتب ذلك العين فعن ابي حنيفة رواه ابويوسف انه اذا اداه لا يعتق وعلى هذه الرواية لم ينعقد العقد الا اذا قال له اذا اديت الى فانتحر فحينئذ يعتق بحكم الشرط وهكذا عن ابى يوسف وعنه انه يعتق قال ذلك اولم يقل لان العقد ينعقد مع الفساد لكون المسمى مالا فيعتق باداء المشروط ولو كاتبه على عين في يد المكاتب فقيه روايتان وهى مسألة الكتابة على الاعيان وقد عُرف ذلك في الاصل وقد ذكرنا وجه الروايتين في كفاية المنتهى
ترجمہ پھر اگر مالک مین نے اس کو جائز رکھا تو امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ عقد جائز ہو جائے گا کیونکہ بوقت اجازت بیع جائز ہو جاتی ہے تو کتابت بدرجہ اولی جائز ہو جائے گی اور امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ جائز نہ ہوگا عدم اجازت کی حالت پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے جیسا کہ کتاب میں مذکور ہے۔ اور امر جامع دونوں میں یہ ہے کہ ایسی اجازت کمائیوں کی ملک ثابت ہونے کا فائدہ نہیں دیتی۔ حالانکہ یہی مقصود ہے کیونکہ کتابت ثابت ہوتی ہے کمائیوں سے ادائیگی ضرورت کی وجہ سے اور جب عوض معین مال ہو تو اسکی ضرورت نہیں اور مسئلہ اسی صورت میں ہے۔ جیسا کہ ہم نے بیان کیا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ عقد جائز ہے۔ مالک اجازت دے یا نہ دے صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ اجازت کی صورت میں اس کی قیمت کا سپرد کرنالازم ہو گا۔ جیسے نکاح میں ہوتا ہے۔ اور امر جامع ان دونوں میں تسمیہ کا صحیح ہوتا ہے اس کے مال ہونے کی وجہ سے، اور اگر مکاتب اس مال مین کا مالک ہو گیا۔ تو امام ابوحنیفہ سے امام ابو یوسف نے روایت کی کہ اس کے آزاد کرنے سے آزاد ہو گا ۔ اس روایت پر عقد منعقد نہ ہوگا۔ مگر جب ہی کہ آقا نے یہ کہا ہو ۔ اذا ادیت الی فانت حر ۔ پس اس صورت
Book of Kitabah. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu Commentary of Hidaya Vol. 12. And from Abu Hanifa, Hasan narrated that the contract is valid, such that if the slave becomes its owner and gives it to the master, he becomes free; and if he becomes incapable, he is made a slave again. Because the specified item is wealth and the ability to deliver is uncertain, so it resembles the dower. We say: In commutative contracts, the specific item (ayn) is the subject matter (ma'qud alayh), and ability over the subject matter is a condition for the validity of the contract when the contract is rescindable, as in sale. Unlike the dower in marriage, because in marriage the ability over what is intended is not a condition, so for the dower which is subordinate, ability is even more not a condition. Commentary on his statement 'on a specific thing belonging to another' ... The word 'li-ghayrihi' is a circumstantial accusative (hal) from the word 'shay', and 'shay' is indefinite which cannot be the subject of the hal. But here it is specified by the attribute 'bi'aynihi', so it becomes valid to be the subject. The issue is: if the master makes kitabah with a slave on a specific thing belonging to another person, e.g., a horse, cloth, or slave, then according to us and Imam Shafi'i and Ahmad, this is invalid because the slave is unable to deliver another's property. According to Imam Malik, it is valid; the slave buys that thing and gives it, and if the owner does not sell, he pays its value. His statement 'and his intent is something...' - Imam Muhammad intends by the word 'shay' in 'ala shay bi'aynihi something that becomes determinate by specification, like cloth, this horse, this slave, this house, etc. And if that thing is not determinate, like if he said 'I made kitabah with you on these one thousand dirhams' while that thousand dirhams belongs to another, the kitabah contract is valid because dirhams and dinars become determinate in trust and usurpation, but not in commutative contracts. So the kitabah contract pertains to those dirhams which are a debt upon the slave. According to Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad, in this case too kitabah is not valid because with them dirhams and dinars are also determinate. His statement 'Hasan narrated it' - The explanation of the issue is that there are two cases in making kitabah on another's property: the thing is determinate by specification, like a horse, slave, etc., or it is not determinate, like currency i.e., dirhams and dinars. The first has two cases: the owner permits it or not. If he does not permit, then two cases: the slave either becomes its owner through some means and delivers it to the master, or not. So there are four total cases. If the thing is not determinate by specification, the kitabah contract is valid, as explained in the previous statement. And if it is determinate and the owner does not permit and the slave cannot become its owner through any means, then in Zahir al-Riwayah it is not valid, and in Hasan's narration it is valid. Now, if the slave acquires ownership of that thing and gives it to the master, he becomes free, and if he cannot give it, he is made a slave, because the specified item is wealth and the ability to deliver is uncertain (based on the probability of acquiring ownership), so the kitabah compensation from another's property resembles the dower of a woman which comes from another's property. For example, if someone marries a woman with a slave belonging to another, the specification is valid; now if the slave's owner does not permit, the woman takes the slave's value from the husband, not the mahr mithl; if the specification were invalid, she would revert to mahr mithl. His statement 'we said that the ayn...' - The reason for Zahir al-Riwayah is that in commutative contracts, the specific item (the kitabah compensation) is the subject matter, and for the validity of the contract, ability over the subject matter is a condition when the contract is rescindable, as in sale. The objection passed earlier that the kitabah compensation has the same ruling as the price in sale, and on that basis kitabah with currency was valid, and the price is the subject matter of the contract? No, the price is not the subject matter, so ability over it cannot be a condition. The answer: the kitabah compensation has the ruling of price only when it is currency, and our discussion is about specific items; in case of a specific item, the kitabah contract is like a muqabada (barter exchange), and the kitabah compensation has the ruling of the sold item, not of the price. His statement 'unlike the dower' - In Hasan's narration, the response to 'so it resembles the dower' is that unlike the dower in marriage, for validity of specification in marriage, it is only required that the specified item be valuable wealth; ability to deliver is not a condition. Because in marriage, the primary purpose - procreation (or according to the author of al-Nihaya, the benefit of the vulva) - ability over it is not a condition, to the extent that marriage with a breastfeeding infant is valid (even though ability is non-existent). So what is not intended but is subordinate, i.e., the dower, ability over it is a fortiori not a condition. If the owner of the item permits it, then is it valid or not? So if the owner permits that, then from Muhammad it is narrated that it is valid, because sale becomes valid upon permission, so kitabah is even more valid. From Abu Hanifa it is narrated that it is not valid, analogizing to the case of no permission, as stated in the book. The common point between them is that such permission does not benefit the slave's ownership, which is the purpose because kitabah is established for the need of payment, and there is no need when the compensation is a specific determinate item, and the issue is as we explained. From Abu Yusuf it is narrated that it is valid whether the owner permits or not, except that with permission, delivery of the specific item is obligatory, and without it, delivery of its value is obligatory, as in marriage. The common point between them is the validity of specification because it is wealth. And if the slave becomes owner of that specific item, from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf narrated that if he pays it, he is not freed. According to this narration, the contract is not concluded unless the master said 'If you pay to me, then you are free' - in that case he becomes free by virtue of the condition. This is also from Abu Yusuf, and from him (another narration) that he becomes free whether he said that or not, because the contract is concluded despite its invalidity due to the specified item being wealth, so he becomes free by paying what was stipulated. And if he (master) made kitabah with him on a specific item that is in the slave's possession, there are two narrations, and this is the issue of kitabah on specific items, which is known in the principle, and we have mentioned the basis of the two narrations in Kifayat al-Muntaha. Translation: Then if the owner of the item permitted it, from Muhammad it is narrated that the contract becomes valid because sale becomes valid at the time of permission, so kitabah is even more valid. And from Abu Hanifa it is narrated that it will not be valid, analogizing to the state of no permission, as mentioned in the book. The common point between the two is that such permission does not benefit the slave's ownership, while this is the purpose because kitabah is established for the need of payment, and there is no need when the compensation is a specific item, and the issue is as we explained. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that the contract is valid whether the owner permits or not, except that in case of permission, delivery of its 'ayn is obligatory, and without it, delivery of its value is obligatory, as in marriage. The common point between them is that the specification is valid because it is wealth. And if the slave becomes owner of that specific item, from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf narrated that he is not freed by paying it. According to this narration, the contract is not concluded unless the master said 'If you pay to me, then you are free' - in that case he becomes free by virtue of the condition. And similarly from Abu Yusuf, and from him (another narration) that he becomes free whether he said that or not, because the contract is concluded despite its invalidity because the specified item is wealth, so he becomes free by paying what was stipulated.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya explains the Hanafi rulings on a mukatab contract (kitabah) where the master stipulates a specific item (ayn) owned by a third party as the compensation for the slave's freedom. The commentary begins by noting a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad (nawadir) that such a contract is valid, with the slave becoming free if he acquires and delivers the item, but returning to slavery if unable. The Hanafi relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah), however, is that the contract is invalid because in commutative contracts (mu'awadat), the subject matter (ma'qud alayh) must be deliverable; inability to deliver renders the contract void. This is analogized to sale, where delivery of the sold item is a condition. The passage contrasts this with mahr in marriage, where delivery of the dower is not a condition because the primary purpose (procreation) does not require immediate delivery, so the subordinate dower similarly has no delivery condition. The text then details the inter-madhhab dispute: the Hanafi and Shafi'i/Ahmad positions hold the contract invalid, while Malik allows it with the slave buying or paying value. It distinguishes between determinate items (like a specific horse) and indeterminate currency (dirhams/dinara), where kitabah on another's currency is valid in Hanafi law because currency does not become specifically determined in commutative contracts (though it does in trust/ghasb). For Shafi'i, currency is also determinate and thus invalid. The passage then explores four scenarios under 'رواه الحسن': whether the item is determinate or not, whether the owner permits, and whether the slave acquires it. In Zahir al-Riwayah, if the item is determinate and no permission and no acquisition, the contract is invalid; in Hasan's narration it is valid and resembles mahr. The master's permission leads to an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad holds it valid, Abu Hanifa invalid (by qiyas on no permission), and Abu Yusuf valid but requiring delivery of the item if permitted, or value if not. Finally, if the slave acquires the item, Abu Hanifa (as narrated by Abu Yusuf) says he does not become free unless the master explicitly conditioned freedom upon payment; another narration from Abu Yusuf says he becomes free regardless. This reflects the tension between the contract being inherently invalid but the specified item being wealth so payment may still effect freedom by condition.

Key Terms
کتابت (kitābah): A contract between a master and his slave whereby the slave agrees to pay a specified sum or deliver a specified item in exchange for his freedom.
مکاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract with his master.
عين (ʿayn): A specific, tangible object that is individually determined (as opposed to currency or fungibles).
معقود عليه (maʿqūd ʿalayh): The subject matter of a contract; that which is contracted upon.
مهر (mahr): The dower given by the husband to the wife in marriage, which is a condition of the contract.
فاسد (fāsid): Invalid or voidable; in Hanafi contract law, a fasid contract is one that is defective but can be corrected if the defect is removed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah), what is the ruling if a master makes a kitabah contract with his slave for a specific horse owned by a third party, and the owner does not permit?
A) The contract is valid and the slave must buy the horse or pay its value.
B) The contract is invalid because the subject matter is not deliverable.
C) The contract is valid because kitabah is like mahr in marriage.
D) The contract is suspended pending the owner's permission.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position holds that kitabah on a specific item owned by a third party is invalid because the slave cannot guarantee delivery at the time of contract, analogized to sale and distinguished from dower.

Kitaba with Condition of Returning an Unspecified Slave: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kitaba condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani invalidate a kitaba contract with a condition of returning an unspecified slave, and distinguish their reasoning from that of Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A condition that excludes value, not a specific item, invalidates the kitaba contract.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute over a specific kitaba condition. The master makes his slave a mukatib for 100 dinars on condition that the master will give him an unspecified slave. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule the contract invalid (fasid), while Abu Yusuf considers it valid by apportioning the dinars. Understanding their reasoning deepens your grasp of the principle that countervalues must be valid substitutes in contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
The act is kitaba (contract of manumission by installment). The condition is that the master will give the mukatib an unspecified (ghayr mu'ayyan) slave in return.
The condition is added to the kitaba contract.
2
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad)
They rule the kitaba invalid (fasid) because the condition effectively excludes the value of the slave, not the slave itself, and value is not a valid substitute in contracts.
The contract is void due to an invalid exclusion of the countervalue.
3
State the opposing view (Abu Yusuf)
Abu Yusuf holds the kitaba valid. He argues that the 100 dinars can be apportioned between the value of the mukatib and the value of an average slave. The portion for the slave is void, and the mukatib becomes free for the remainder.
He considers an absolute slave a valid substitute, so the exclusion is of a slave, not its value.
4
Analyze the proofs
Abu Yusuf's proof: an absolute slave is suitable as a substitute in kitaba, so it can be an excluded item. The Hanafi majority response: the condition does not exclude a specific slave; it excludes the value of a slave, and value is not a valid substitute. Hence the exclusion is invalid.
The key difference: what is actually excluded — the slave or its value.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If the mukatib pays the full 100 dinars, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, he is not freed (contract invalid). According to Abu Yusuf, he would be freed after paying the apportioned amount (100 minus the value of an average slave).
The practical effect depends on which view is followed.
6
Identify the mufta bihi (relied-upon position)
The position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the majority view; it is the mufta bihi. Abu Yusuf's view is a rare transmission.
For fatwa, the ruling is that such a kitaba is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وان كاتبه على مائة دينار على ان يرد المولى اليه عبدا بغير عينه فالكتابة فاسدة عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد وقال ابويوسف هي جائزة ويقسم المائة الدينار على قيمة المكاتب وعلى قيمة عبد وسط فتبطل منها حصة العبد فيكون مكاتبا بما بقى لان العبد المطلق يصلح بدل الكتابة وينصرف الى الوسط فكذا يصلح مستثنى منه وهو الاصل في ابدال العقود ولهما انه لا يستثنى العبد من الدنانير وإنما يستثنى قيمته والقيمة لا تصلح بدلا فكذلک مستثنی
He said: And if he made him a mukatib for one hundred dinars on condition that the master give him a slave undetermined, then the kitaba is invalid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said: It is valid, and the one hundred dinars are apportioned between the value of the mukatib and the value of an average slave, so the portion of the slave is void, and he becomes a mukatib for the remainder, because an absolute slave is suitable as a substitute for kitaba and is referred to the average, so similarly it is suitable as an excluded item, and this is the principle in exchanges of contracts. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): He does not exclude the slave from the dinars; rather he excludes its value, and value is not suitable as a substitute, so similarly it is not suitable as an excluded item.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a kitaba contract where the master makes his slave a mukatib for 100 dinars on the condition that the master will give the slave an unspecified (undetermined) slave. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani rule that the kitaba is invalid (fasid), while Abu Yusuf holds it as valid. Abu Yusuf's reasoning is that the 100 dinars should be divided proportionally between the value of the mukatib himself (to determine his freedom price) and the value of an average slave (the non-specific slave to be returned). The portion allocated to the slave is void, and the mukatib is freed for the remainder. He argues that an absolute slave is valid as a substitute in kitaba (like the price for freedom), so it can also be an excluded item. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad respond that the slave is not being excluded from the dinars; rather, its value is excluded, and value is not a valid substitute in such contracts, so the exclusion is invalid. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as it aligns with the principle that the countervalue must be known and valid.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitaba contract with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
كتابة (kitaba): A contract of manumission by which a slave is promised freedom upon paying a specified sum.
استثناء (istithna'): Exclusion of an item from the countervalue in a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid because the slave is a valid substitute.
B) Invalid because the value is excluded, and value is not a valid substitute.
C) Valid by istihsan.
D) Invalid only if the slave is not average.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a kitaba contract is invalid if the condition requires the master to give an unspecified slave, because the condition effectively excludes value, not a specific item, and value is not a valid substitute.

Kitaba on Unspecified Animal: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Inter-madhhab dispute on kitaba with genus-only specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates kitaba on an unspecified animal by istihsan, and evaluate the Shafi'i qiyas objection.

Core Idea
Kitaba is based on indulgence (musamaha), not haggling (mumaqassa), so slight ignorance in specifying the countervalue is tolerated.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a key methodological difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding kitaba (contract of manumission). The Hanafi school permits a kitaba where the slave agrees to pay an animal specified only by genus (e.g., a horse, not a specific horse), using istihsan. The Shafi'i school rejects this, insisting on strict specification by qiyas to sale. Understanding this dispute reveals the Hanafi view that kitaba is closer to marriage than to sale.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: kitaba on an animal specified only by genus is valid by istihsan. Note that the slave must pay the average value of that genus.
The contract is not void even though the exact animal is unknown.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its qiyas basis
Imam al-Shafi'i holds the contract invalid. He uses qiyas: kitaba is an exchange (mu'awada), so it must be treated like sale, which requires precise specification to avoid gharar.
This is a straight analogy to the strict rules of sale.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response (istihsan + analogy to nikah)
Hanafis argue that kitaba is not a pure exchange; it is a contract that voids the master's ownership gradually, similar to nikah (marriage). Nikah tolerates slight ignorance (e.g., unspecified dower). Therefore, qiyas to sale is inappropriate.
The common link is musamaha (indulgence), which governs both kitaba and nikah.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Hanafis, the contract is binding; the slave must pay the average value. According to Shafi'is, the contract is void from the start.
This affects whether the slave can gain freedom through such a contract.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in the school, based on istihsan and the principle of musamaha.
The text itself presents istihsan as the basis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و اذا كاتبه على حيوان غير موصوف فالكتابة جائزة استحسانا ومعناه ان يبين الجنس ولا يبين النوع والصفة وينصرف الى الوسط ويجبر على قبول القيمة وقد مر فى النكاح اما اذا لم يبين الجنس مثل ان يقول دابة لا يجوز لانه يشمل اجناسا مختلفة فيتفاحش الجهالة واذا بين الجنس كالعبد والوصيف فالجهالة يسيرة ومثلها يتحمل فى الكتابة فيعتبر جهالة البدل بجهالة الاجل فيه وقال الشافعى لا يجوز وهو القياس لانه معاوضة فاشبه البيع ولنا انه معاوضة مال بغير مال او مال لكن على وجه يسقط الملك فيه فاشبه النكاح والجامع انه يبتنى على المسامحة بخلاف البيع لان مبناه على المماكسة
He said: And if he made him a mukatib on an animal unspecified (in type and description), the kitaba is valid by istihsan. Its meaning is that he specifies the genus but does not specify the type and description, and it is referred to the average, and he is compelled to accept the value. This has already passed in nikah. As for when he does not specify the genus, such as saying 'an animal', it is not valid because it includes different genera, and ignorance becomes grave. And when he specifies the genus, such as 'a slave' or 'a servant', the ignorance is slight, and such ignorance is tolerated in kitaba, so ignorance of the countervalue is considered by analogy to ignorance of the term. And al-Shafi'i said: It is not valid, and this is the qiyas because it is an exchange, so it resembles sale. And for us: It is an exchange of property for property, but in such a way that ownership is voided, so it resembles nikah, and the common link is that it is based on indulgence, unlike sale which is based on haggling.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of kitaba when the countervalue is an animal whose species (jins) is mentioned but its type and description are not specified (ghayr mawsuf). According to the Hanafi school, this contract is valid by istihsan (juristic preference). The reasoning is that it is similar to the nikah contract, where such ambiguity is tolerated. The mukatab must give the average of that genus, and the master is compelled to accept its value. However, if the species is not even mentioned (e.g., saying 'dābba' which includes different animals), the contract is invalid due to gross ignorance. When the species is specified, the ignorance is slight and acceptable in kitaba. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding it invalid by qiyas because kitaba is an exchange (mu'awada) resembling sale, where specification is required. The Hanafi response distinguishes kitaba from sale: in kitaba, the master's ownership over the slave is gradually being relinquished, similar to marriage where speculation is tolerated; hence it is based on musamaha (indulgence), not mumaqassa (haggling) like sale. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas in the Hanafi school when justice or custom demands it.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to derive rulings from primary sources.
مسامحة (musamaha): Indulgence or tolerance; a characteristic that allows slight ignorance in contracts like kitaba and nikah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the animal can be physically examined later.
B) Because kitaba resembles nikah, which tolerates slight ignorance.
C) Because the master can always set the price later.
D) Because qiyas to sale permits it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi validation of kitaba on genus-only animal demonstrates the school's use of istihsan to override qiyas when the underlying nature of the contract (indulgence) demands it.

Slight Ignorance in Kitaba: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on jahala yasira in kitaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school tolerates slight ignorance in kitaba and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i position, using the concepts of istihsan and analogy.

Core Idea
Kitaba tolerates slight ignorance because it resembles nikah in leniency, not bay' in strictness.

This passage addresses a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether a kitaba contract (where a slave buys freedom by paying installments) is valid if there is slight ignorance (jahala yasira) regarding the payment term or description of the consideration. The Hanafi school holds that such ignorance is tolerable, drawing an analogy to nikah (marriage), where slight uncertainty in the dower is permitted. The Shafi'i school, by contrast, treats kitaba as a pure exchange contract (mu'awada) like bay' (sale), where any ignorance in the price or term invalidates the contract. The commentator explains the Hanafi proof, which relies on istihsan (juristic preference) over strict qiyas.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: kitaba is valid (sahih) even if there is slight ignorance in the description or term of the consideration. The example given is 'until the harvest' – an unspecified term.
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad hold that any ignorance, even slight, invalidates kitaba, because kitaba is a contract of exchange like bay'.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i qiyas: kitaba is an exchange of property for property (mu'awada maliyya), so it must follow the strict rules of sale – ignorance in price or term nullifies.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine how the Hanafi school rebuts this: they argue that kitaba has two aspects – initially it is a exchange of property for non-property (fakk al-hajr), and ultimately it is like nikah where ownership drops. The common element is leniency (tasamuh), not strictness. Thus qiyas to bay' is rejected by istihsan.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Hanafi, a kitaba with an unspecified term like 'until the harvest' is valid; under Shafi'i, it is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله فيعتبر جهالة ... الخ - بدل کتابت کی خفیف جہالت کا قیاس میعاد کے مجہول ہونے پر ہے کہ کتابت میں اگر اداء بدل کی میعاد مجہول ہو ۔ بان قال كاتبتك الى الحصاد تو عقد کتابت صحیح ہوتا ہے۔ اس کو قدرے توضیح کیساتھ یوں سمجھو کہ کتابت بائیں لحاظ کہ معاوضہ مال بلا مال ہے مشابہ نکاح ہے اور بائیں لحاظ کہ معاوضہ مال بالمال ہے۔ مشابہ بیج ہے۔ پس اگر جنس مجہول ہو تو جائز نہ ہوگا اور اگر نوع و وصف مجہول ہو تو یہ جہالت چونکہ بیرہ ہے۔ اس لئے نکاح کی طرح کتابت میں بھی قابل تحمل ہے۔ قوله وقال الشافعي ... الخ - امام شافعی واحمد کے یہاں جہالت بیرہ سے بھی کتابت جائز نہ ہوگی ۔ قیاس بھی یہی ہے کیونکہ کتابت معاوضہ مال بالمال ہونے کی بناء پر ایک عقد معاوضہ ہے تو بیع کے مشابہ ہوا اور بدل یا میعاد مجہول ہونے کی صورت میں بیچ صحیح نہیں ہوتی تو کتابت بھی صحیح نہ ہوگی ۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کتابت معاوضہ مال بلا مال ہے۔ کیونکہ بدل کتابت ابتداء میں فکتِ حجر کے مقابلہ میں ہوتا ہے اور فک حجر مال نہیں ہے۔ یا کتابت معاوضہ مال بالمال ہی ہے کیونکہ بدل کتابت انتہاء رقبہ کے مقابلہ میں ہوتا ہے لیکن یہ ایسے طور پر ہے کہ اس میں ملکیت آقا کے لئے ساقط ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے کہ غلام اپنی ذات کی مالیت کا مالک نہیں ہوتا۔ پس یہ نکاح کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ کہ منافع بضع دخول کے وقت مال ہیں تو یہ بھی معاوضہ مال بالمال ہوا۔ چنانچہ شریعت نے منافع کو اعیان کے درجہ میں رکھا ہے۔ لیکن مال ہونا ایسے طور پر ہے کہ ملک زوج کے لئے ساقط ہوتی ہے۔
ولهذا لا يقدر على تمليكها اور کتابت و نکاح میں جامع دونوں میں نرمی مقصود ہوتی ہے۔ بخلاف بیچ کے کہ وہ ختی وتنگی پر بنی ہے لہذا کتابت کو بیچ پر قیاس کرنا صحیح نہیں۔
His saying: 'So ignorance is considered...' - The analogy of slight ignorance of the consideration in kitaba is based on the ignorance of the term. For in kitaba, if the term of payment is unknown, such as saying 'I have made kitaba with you until the harvest,' then the contract of kitaba is valid. Understand this with some explanation: Kitaba, from one aspect being an exchange of property for non-property, resembles nikah, and from another aspect being an exchange of property for property, resembles bay'. Thus, if the type is unknown, it is not permissible, but if the species and description are unknown, such ignorance is slight. Therefore, like nikah, it is tolerabled in kitaba. His saying: 'And al-Shafi'i said...' - According to Imam Shafi'i and Ahmad, even slight ignorance makes kitaba impermissible. This is also the analogy, because kitaba, being an exchange of property for property, is a contract of exchange, so it resembles bay'. In the case of unknown consideration or term, bay' is not valid, so kitaba would also not be valid. Our proof is that kitaba is an exchange of property for non-property, because the consideration of kitaba in the beginning is in exchange for fakk al-hajr (removal of restriction), and fakk al-hajr is not property. Or kitaba is an exchange of property for property, because the consideration of kitaba in the end is in exchange for the slave's person, but such that the ownership of the master is dropped, because the slave does not own his own value. Thus it resembles nikah, because the benefits of the vulva at the time of entry are property, so this too is an exchange of property for property. Indeed, the Shariah has placed benefits in the category of tangible goods. But property is such that the ownership of the husband is dropped. Therefore, he is not able to make her property. And in kitaba and nikah, the common point is that leniency is intended in both, unlike bay', which is based on strictness and hardship. Hence, analogizing kitaba to bay' is not correct.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on whether slight ignorance (jahala yasira) in the consideration or term of a kitaba contract invalidates it. The Hanafi position, as presented by the commentator, is that such ignorance is tolerabled. The reasoning is that kitaba has two aspects: it resembles nikah (marriage) in that it is a transition from one status to another with leniency, and it resembles bay' (sale) in that it involves exchange. However, because the primary purpose is leniency and removing the slave from restriction, it is more akin to nikah. Therefore, slight ignorance in the description (not the type) of the consideration or in the term is permitted. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad argue that kitaba is purely an exchange contract and thus any ignorance invalidates it, just as in bay'. The Hanafi response is that this qiyas (analogy) is overridden by istihsan (juristic preference) because the spirit of kitaba is leniency, not strictness. The commentator explains that the consideration in kitaba initially corresponds to the breaking of the master's ownership right (fakk al-hajr), which is not property, and ultimately to the slave's person in a way that ownership drops, similar to the marriage contract where the husband pays the dower for exclusive right to the wife's vulva, but the ownership of the vulva is not transferred. Thus, kitaba is a unique contract requiring leniency.

Key Terms
کتابت (kitābah): A contract between a master and a slave whereby the slave agrees to pay a specified amount to the master in exchange for freedom.
جہالت (jahālah): Ignorance about the type, description, or term of the consideration in a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is slight ignorance (jahala yasira) in the consideration or term of kitaba tolerated?
A) Because kitaba is like bay' where ignorance is always invalid.
B) Because kitaba resembles nikah where slight ignorance is tolerated, and leniency is intended.
C) Because the slave is not a competent party.
D) Because the Quran explicitly permits it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school tolerates slight ignorance in kitaba because the contract is built on leniency, similar to nikah, and istihsan overrides strict qiyas to bay'.

Kitaba upon Wine by a Christian
Ruling and analysis of Christian’s kitaba upon wine

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kitaba with wine by non-Muslims, explain the istihsan basis, and apply the substitution of value upon conversion.

Core Idea
Wine is property for non-Muslims; their kitaba remains valid even after conversion by substituting value.

The Hanafi school uniquely recognizes wine as property (mal) for non-Muslims, allowing contracts like kitaba where the consideration is wine. This passage from al-Hidayah explains the ruling, its conditions, the shift to value if one party embraces Islam, and distinguishes it from ordinary sale. The principle of istihsan provides the foundation: recognizing their religious transactions unless fundamentally contrary to Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is kitaba (contract of manumission by payment) between a Christian master and his Christian slave, with wine as the consideration (badal). The ruling is that it is valid (sahih).
The master is Christian; the slave must be a disbeliever.
2
Note the conditions
Two conditions are required: (1) the amount of wine must be known (to avoid gharar), and (2) the slave must be a disbeliever (not Muslim).
Ignorance of the consideration would invalidate the contract.
3
Understand the istihsan dalil
The proof is based on istihsan: wine is property (mal) in the legal system of non-Muslims, just as vinegar is property for Muslims. Therefore, their transaction is recognized by Shariah.
This is a departure from strict qiyas, which would consider wine non-property.
4
Analyze the conversion scenario
If either the master or the slave converts to Islam after the contract, the consideration automatically converts to the value (qimah) of the wine, since a Muslim cannot lawfully own or deliver wine. The contract remains valid and the slave gains freedom upon paying the value.
Value substitution is specific to kitaba, not sale.
5
Compare with sale between dhimmis
If two dhimmis sell wine and one converts, the sale becomes invalid (fasid) because a sale cannot be completed with value. In kitaba, value can substitute, due to the lenient nature of the contract (it is built on flexibility).
This distinction highlights the unique fiqh of kitaba.

قال و اذا كاتب النصرانى عبده على خمر فهو جائز معناه اذا كان مقدارا معلوما والعبد كافرا لانها مال في حقهم بمنزلة الخل في حقنا وايهما اسلم فللمولى قيمة الخمر لان المسلم ممنوع عن تملیک الخمر وتملكها وفى التسليم ذلك اذ الخمر غیر متعین فيعجز عن تسليم البدل فيجب عليه قيمته وهذا بخلاف ما اذا تبايع الذميان خمرا ثم اسلم احدهما حيث يفسد البيع على ما قاله البعض لان القيمة تصلح بدلا في الكتابة في الجملة فانه لو كاتب على وصيف واتى بالقيمة يجبر على القبول فجاز ان يبقى العقد على القيمة اما البيع لا ينعقد صحيحا على القيمة فافترقا قال واذا قبضها عتق لان فى الكتابة معنى المعاوضة فاذا وصل احد العوضين الى المولى سلم العوض الآخر للعبد وذلك بالعتق بخلاف ما اذا كان العبد مسلما حيث لم يجز الكتابة لان المسلم ليس من اهل التزام الخمر ولو اداها عتق وقد بيناه من قبل والله اعلم ترجمہ اگر مکاتب کیا نصرانی نے اپنے غلام کو شراب پر تو یہ جائز ہے۔ اس کے معنی یہ ہیں۔ کہ شراب کی مقدار معلوم اور غلام کافر ہو۔ کیونکہ شلاب ان کے حق میں مال ہے۔ جیسے سر کہ ہمارے حق میں۔ اور ان میں سے جو مسلمان ہو جائے تو آقا کے لئے شراب کی قیمت ہوگی کیونکہ مسلمان کو شراب کی تملیک و تملک سے روکا گیا ہے اور سپر د کرنے میں یہ بات موجود ہے اس لئے کہ شراب متعین نہیں تو تسلیم عوض سے عاجز ہوگا۔ لہذا اس پر قیمت واجب ہو گی۔ اور یہ اس کے خلاف ہے۔ جب روز میوں نے شراب کی خرید و فروخت کی ۔ پھر ان میں سے کوئی مسلمان ہو گیا کہ بقول بعض بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ کتابت میں قیمت فی الجملہ ہو سکتی ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر غلام کو خدمتی چھوکری پر مکاتب کیا اور مکاتب اس کی قیمت لایا تو آقا کو اس کے لینے پر مجبور کیا جائیگا۔ پس جائز ہے کہ عقد قیمت پر باقی رہے۔ رہی بیع سو وہ وقت پیچ منعقد نہیں ہوتی۔ پس دونوں میں فرق ہو گیا۔ اور جب آقا نے شراب پر قبضہ کر لیا تو غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ کتابت میں معاوضہ کے معنی ہیں۔ پس جب ایک عوض آقا کو پہنچ گیا تو دوسرا عوض غلام کے لئے مسلم ہوگا اور یہ آزاد ہو جانے سے ہوگا۔ بخلاف اس کے جہ غلام مسلمان ہو کہ کتابت جائز نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ مسلمان اہل التزام خمر سے نہیں ہے اور اگر اس نے شراب ادا کر دی تو آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ تشریح قوله واذا كاتب النصراني ... الخ - اگر کسی نصرانی نے اپنے غلام کو شراب پر مکاتب کیا تو یہ جائز ہے بشرطیکہ شراب کی مقدار معلوم ہو۔ کیونکہ جہالت بدل مانع جواز ہوتی ہے۔ نیز غلام کا فر ہو۔ اگر مسلمان ہو تو کتابت بدل مذکور کی ادائیگی کے ساتھ عشق کی تعلیق کا مضمن ہے تو یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کسی مسلمان نے اپنے مسلم غلام کو شراب پر مکاتب کیا اور مکاتب نے شراب ادا کر دی تو وہ آزاد ہو جاتا ہے۔ قاضی ظہیر الدین ، رازی، نجم الدین افضلی اور نیشا پوری وغیرہ مشائخ نے ایسا ہی ذکر کیا ہے البتہ شرح طحاوی وتمر ناشی میں ہے کہ آزاد نہ ہوگا۔
قـولـه ومعناه اذا كان .... الخ - یہ دونوں شرطیں عبارت جامع صغیر میں مصرح موجود ہیں مگر صاحب ہدایہ نے یہاں جامع کی عبارت بعینہ ذکر نہیں کی۔ اس لئے دونوں شرطوں پر متنبہ کرنے کی ضرورت پیش آئی۔
قوله لانها مال .. الخ - مذکورہ کتابت کے جواز کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ شراب ان لوگوں کے حق میں ایسا مال ہے جیسے ہمارے حق میں سرکہ مال ہے۔ پھر آقا اور مکاتب میں سے جو کوئی مسلمان ہو جائے ۔ تو ہر حال میں آقا کو شراب کی قیمت ملے گی۔ (امام شافعی و مالک ، ایک روایت میں امام احمد ومحمد کے نزدیک کتابت فاسد ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ مسلمان کو شراب کی تملیک ( مالک بنانے اور مالک ہونے ) ہے منع کیا گیا ہے اور شراب سپرد کرنے میں یہی لازم آتا ہے۔ یعنی اگر مکاتب مسلمان ہوا تو تملیک اور آقا مسلمان ہوا تو تملک لازم آتا ہے کیونکہ مسئلہ میں مفروض یہی ہے کہ شراب غیر معین ہے تو اس میں ملک نفس عقد سے ثابت نہ ہوگی بلکہ سپرد کرنے سے ثابت ہوگی (برخلاف اس کے جب شراب معین ہو۔ کہ اس میں نفس عقد سے ملک ثابت ہو جائے گی اور اب شرب سپرد کرنا ایک قبضہ سے دوسرے قبضہ کی طرف منتقل کرنا ہوگا۔ اور مسلمان کے لئے نقل ید ممنوع نہیں ہے ) بہر کیف جب مسلمان کے لئے تسلیم خمرممنوع ہوا تو وہ بدل کتابت سپرد کرنے سے عاجز ہو گیا۔ لہذا اس کی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔
He said: If a Christian makes kitaba with his slave upon wine, it is valid. Its meaning is when the amount is known and the slave is a disbeliever, because it (wine) is property in their regard, like vinegar in our regard. And whichever of them becomes Muslim, for the master is the value of the wine, because the Muslim is prohibited from making ownership of wine and owning it, and in delivery that is present because the wine is unspecified, so he becomes unable to deliver the consideration; thus its value is obligatory upon him. And this is contrary to when two dhimmis trade wine then one of them becomes Muslim, where the sale becomes invalid according to some, because value is suitable as a consideration in kitaba in the absolute sense. For if he made kitaba upon a slave-girl and he brought the value, the master is compelled to accept, so it is permissible that the contract remain on the value. As for sale, it is not valid on value, so they differ. He said: If he takes possession of it, the slave is freed, because in kitaba is the meaning of exchange; so when one of the considerations reaches the master, the other consideration is secured for the slave, and that is by emancipation. Contrary to when the slave is Muslim, where kitaba is not valid because the Muslim is not of the people of undertaking wine; but if he gives it, he is freed, and we have explained it before. And Allah knows best. Translation: If a Christian makes his slave a mukatab upon wine, it is valid. Its meaning is that the wine's amount is known and the slave is a disbeliever, because wine is property in their right, like vinegar in our right. And whichever of them becomes Muslim, then the master will have the value of the wine, because the Muslim is prohibited from making someone else owner of wine and from owning it, and in delivery this exists, because wine is unspecified, so he is unable to deliver the consideration; hence its value becomes obligatory. And this is contrary to when two dhimmis buy and sell wine, then one of them becomes Muslim, for the sale becomes invalid according to some, because value is suitable as a consideration in kitaba in the absolute sense. So if he made kitaba upon a serving girl and the mukatab brought her value, the master is compelled to accept it; thus it is permissible that the contract remains on the value. As for sale, it is not valid on value, so they differ. And when the master takes possession of it, the slave becomes free, because in kitaba there is the meaning of exchange. So when one consideration reaches the master, the other consideration is secured for the slave, and that is through freeing. Contrary to when the slave is Muslim, that kitaba is not valid, because the Muslim is not capable of undertaking wine, but if he gives it, he becomes free. Elaboration of his saying: 'If a Christian makes kitaba...' - If a Christian makes kitaba upon his slave with wine, it is valid provided the amount of wine is known, because ignorance of the consideration prevents validity. Also, the slave must be a disbeliever. If the slave is Muslim, then the kitaba includes a suspension of freedom upon payment, so it is like a Muslim making kitaba with his Muslim slave upon wine, and if the mukatab gives the wine, he becomes free. Qadi Zahir al-Din, Razi, Najm al-Din Afzali, Nishapuri and other mashayikh have mentioned similarly. However, in Sharh al-Tahawi and Tamar Nashi, it is that he will not be freed. His saying: 'And its meaning when...' - These two conditions are explicitly present in the phrase of al-Jami' al-Saghir, but the author of al-Hidayah did not quote the phrase of al-Jami' verbatim. Therefore, there is a need to draw attention to the two conditions. His saying: 'Because it is property...' - The reason for the permissibility of the mentioned kitaba is that wine is property in their regard, just as vinegar is property in our regard. Then whichever of the master and the mukatab becomes Muslim, in any case the master will get the value of the wine. (According to Imam Shafi'i and Malik, and in one narration Ahmad and Muhammad, the kitaba becomes invalid because the Muslim is prohibited from making ownership of wine and owning it, and delivering wine necessitates this. That is, if the mukatab becomes Muslim, necessitating tamlik (making owner), and if the master becomes Muslim, necessitating tamalluk (owning), because in the assumed case the wine is unspecified, so ownership is not established by the contract itself but by delivery. (Contrary to when the wine is specified, because ownership is established by the contract itself, and then delivering the wine is merely transferring possession, which is not prohibited for a Muslim.) In any case, when delivering wine is prohibited for a Muslim, he becomes unable to deliver the consideration of kitaba. Hence its value becomes obligatory.)
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on a Christian (Nasarani) making a kitaba contract with his slave using wine as the consideration (badal). The ruling is that it is valid under two conditions: (1) the amount of wine is known, and (2) the slave is a disbeliever (the master is assumed to be Christian). The rationale is that wine is considered property (mal) in the law of non-Muslims, analogous to vinegar for Muslims. This is a concession based on istihsan, recognizing their religious practices. The text then addresses the scenario where one of the parties converts to Islam after the contract. If the master converts, the slave must instead pay the value of the wine, because the Muslim master cannot lawfully receive or own wine. If the slave converts, the master also receives the value, as the slave cannot deliver wine (since it is not property for him). In either case, the contract remains valid and the master is entitled to the value, not the wine itself. The passage also distinguishes kitaba from a sale (bay') between dhimmis: if they sold wine and then one converted, the sale becomes invalid (fasad) because a sale cannot be completed with value; but in kitaba, value can substitute the wine because of the flexible nature of the contract. The author cites a difference of opinion among later scholars: some say the slave does not become free by paying wine after conversion, but the majority (Qadi Zahir al-Din, etc.) affirm freedom. The text also explains that if the slave is Muslim from the start, the kitaba with wine is invalid ab initio because a Muslim cannot undertake to pay wine. However, if he actually pays it, he becomes free according to many scholars, but there is a minority view that he does not. The Halabi (and Hanafiyya) position is that the contract is valid with the value obligation upon conversion.

Key Terms
خمر (khamr): Wine, an intoxicating beverage made from grapes. Considered property (mal) for non-Muslims in this context.
نصرانی (naṣrānī): A Christian; in this context, a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen of the Islamic state) who follows the Christian religion.
قيمة (qīmah): Monetary value; the market price or estimated worth of a commodity. In this case, the value of the wine that must be paid if the contracting parties become Muslims.
كتابة (kitābah): A contract of manumission where a slave agrees to pay a sum (or deliver goods) to the master in exchange for freedom upon payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A Christian master makes a kitaba with his Christian slave upon an amount of wine. The slave converts to Islam before paying. According to the Hanafi school, what happens to the contract and the slave's obligation?
A) The contract becomes invalid, and the slave remains enslaved.
B) The master is entitled to the value of the wine, and the slave is freed upon paying it.
C) The slave is freed immediately without payment.
D) The contract is void ab initio because wine is not property.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates kitaba upon wine between non-Muslims, and upon conversion, value substitutes for the wine, preserving the slave's path to freedom.

If a Mukatab Buys a Non-Lineage Mahram
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kitaba inclusion of a non-lineage mahram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on this issue and apply the Hanafi principle of intermediate relationships to derive the ruling.

Core Idea
A mukatab's purchase of a non-lineage mahram does not enter kitaba because his capacity is limited to kasb, not milk.

In this passage, we encounter an intra-Hanafi dispute about the scope of a mukatab's kitaba. The mukatab—a slave who has contracted with his master to earn his freedom—buys a close relative who is not a direct descendant or ancestor. Does that relative automatically become part of the kitaba? Imam Abu Hanifa says no, while his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, say yes. Their disagreement hinges on the nature of the mukatab's ownership and the analogy to lineage relationships. This lesson will guide you through the reasoning of both sides and the chosen view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
The act is a mukatab buying a dhi rahm mahram who is not related by lineage (wilada). The dispute: does this relative enter into the mukatab's kitaba?
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa's position: the relative does not enter. His proof: the mukatab only has kasb (earning), not milk (ownership). Kasb suffices for sila rahmi only in direct lineage (parent/child). For others, nafaqa is only on the wealthy. Also, the relationship is intermediate—treated like cousins in kitaba and like lineage in emancipation.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Sahibayn's position: the relative does enter, by analogy to lineage relationship. They argue that the obligation of sila rahmi applies to both, and in a free person there is no difference between lineage and non-lineage mahrams regarding freedom. Therefore, they should be treated alike.
4
Analyze the qiyas argument (qiyas khafi)
Abu Hanifa's response uses a refined analogy: the relationship is intermediate. In emancipation (which is quicker), it follows lineage; in kitaba (which is slower and can be rescinded), it follows cousins. This is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) based on the relative strength of the effects.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical difference: if a mukatab buys his sister, according to Abu Hanifa she does not enter kitaba and remains a slave. According to Sahibayn, she enters and benefits from his eventual freedom. The relied-upon view is usually Abu Hanifa's because it is more restrictive.

Source Text
