وان اشترى ذا رحم محرم منه لاولاد له لم يدخل في كتابته عند ابي حنيفة وقالا يدخل اعتبارا بقرابة الولاد واذ وجوب الصلة ينتظمهما ولهذا لا يفترقان فى الحر فى حق الحرية وله ان للمكاتب كسبا لا ملكا غير ان الكسب يكفى للصلة فى الولاد حتى ان القادر على الكسب يخاطب بنفقة الوالد والولد ولا يكفى في غيرهما حتى لا تجب نفقة الاخ الا على الموسر ولان هذه قرابة توسطت بين بنى الاعمام وقرابة الولاد فالحقناها بالثاني في العتق وبالاول في الكتابة وهذا اولى لان العتق اسرع نفوذا من الكتابة حتى ان احد الشريكين اذا كاتب كان للآخر فسخه واذا اعتق لا يكون له فسخه
If he buys a dhi rahm mahram who is not related by lineage (wilada), it does not enter into his kitaba according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it enters, by analogy to lineage relationship because the obligation of maintaining ties includes both, and therefore they do not differ in the case of a free person with respect to freedom. His (Abu Hanifa's) proof is that the mukatab has earning (kasb) but not ownership (milk), except that earning suffices for maintaining ties in lineage relationship such that the one capable of earning is addressed with the nafaqa of parent and child, and it does not suffice for others such that the nafaqa of a brother is only obligatory on the wealthy. And because this relationship is intermediate between cousin relationship and lineage relationship, so we attach it to the latter in emancipation and to the former in kitaba, and this is more appropriate because emancipation has a quicker effect than kitaba; indeed, if one of two partners makes a kitaba, the other can rescind it, but if he frees, he cannot rescind it.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. It presents the matn stating the rule: if a mukatab buys a close relative (dhi rahm mahram) who is not related by lineage (wilada), then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, that relative does not enter into the mukatab's kitaba. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that he does enter, by analogy (qiyas) to lineage relationship. Both agree that maintaining family ties (sila rahmi) is obligatory, but they differ on the extent. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: a mukatab has only kasb (earning) not ownership (milk). Kasb suffices for maintaining ties only in direct lineage (parent-child) because even a capable earner is obligated to provide nafaqa for parents and children. For other relatives, nafaqa is only wajib on the wealthy (musir). Therefore, the analogy does not extend. The Sahibayn argue that the relationship in question is intermediate between cousins (bani al-a'mam) and lineage relations. They compare it to lineage in matters of emancipation (i'taq) because emancipation is quicker in effect: if one partner frees a slave, the other cannot rescind, but if he makes kitaba, the other can rescind. So in emancipation, the ruling is like lineage (they enter), but in kitaba, the ruling is like cousins (they do not enter). This is the preferred view according to the Sahibayn.

Key Terms
ذی رحم محرم (dhi rahm mahram): A relative within the prohibited degrees of marriage, such as a sister, aunt, etc., but who is not a direct descendant or ascendant (i.e., not parent/child).
قرابت ولاد (qarabat wilada): Relationship by lineage/birth, i.e., parents, children, and their descendants.
کسب (kasb): Earnings; the mukatab has the ability to earn but not full ownership (milk) over his person or property beyond his earnings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn in this case?
A) Whether the mukatab can buy the relative at all.
B) Whether the relative enters into the kitaba and benefits from the mukatab's eventual freedom.
C) Whether the relative owes nafaqa to the mukatab.
D) Whether the master can rescind the kitaba.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a mukatab's purchase of a non-lineage mahram does not cause that relative to enter kitaba (Abu Hanifa's view), due to the mukatab's limited capacity (kasb vs milk).

Offspring of a Mukatab Married to a Deceptive Woman
Explains two rulings on mukatab offspring and the dispute between Muhammad and the two shaykhs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the status of children born to a mukatab married to a deceptive woman, explain the proof of each side, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
A child follows the mother in slavery; the free man's exception requires immediate payment, not just deception.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the offspring of a mukatab (or ma'dhun slave) who married a woman falsely claiming to be free. The core question is whether the original principle—that a child's status follows the mother—can be overridden by the father's deception (ghurur), as is done for a free man. We will analyze the reasoning of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad, and understand how the school resolved the conflict.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basic principle
The default rule is that a child follows the mother in slavery or freedom. This applies even if the father is free, unless an exception is established.
This principle is derived from reports and is agreed upon.
2
Note the exception for a free man
When a free man is deceived into marrying a slave woman, the child is freed upon payment of its price. This is based on a Companions' ruling, considered an ijma' by the Hanafi school.
The exception requires immediate (prompt) payment because the free man can pay.
3
Identify the disputed extension
The dispute is whether this exception extends to a mukatab or ma'dhun slave. Imam Muhammad says yes (by qiyas on deception), while the two shaykhs say no.
The thamarah al-khilaf: children belong to owner vs. freed for deferred price.
4
Analyze the proofs
Muhammad argues the 'illa is deception, present in both cases. The shaykhs argue the 'illa is actually immediate payment, which is absent for the mukatab who cannot pay immediately.
The shaykhs maintain that the original principle (child follows mother) remains.
5
Determine the tarjih
The mufta bihi is the view of the two shaykhs, as it is recorded in zahir al-riwayah and Abu Yusuf's final position aligns with Abu Hanifa.
Imam Quduri confirms this tarjih.

كتاب المكاتب الغرور وهذا لانه ما رغب فى نكاحها الا لينال حرية الاولاد ولهما انه مولود بين رقيقين فيكون رقيقا وهذا لان الاصل ان الولد يتبع الام فى الرق والحرية خالفنا هذا الاصل فى الحر باجماع الصحابة وهذا ليس في . معناه لان حق المولى هناک مجبور بقيمة ناجزة وههنا بقيمة متاخرة الى ما بعد العتاق فيبقى على الاصل فلا يلحق به ترجمہ اگر کسی نے اپنی باندی کا نکاح اپنے غلام سے کر دیا پھر ان دونوں کو مکاتب کیا اور باندی نے اس سے بچہ جنا تو یہ بچہ باندی کی کتابت میں داخل ہو جائے گا۔ اور بچہ کی کمائی اس کی ماں کیلئے ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ ماں کے تابع ہونا راجح تر ہے۔ اسی لئے بچہ غلامی اور آزادی میں ماں کا تابع اور غلامی میں اپنی ماں کا تابع ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن فریب خوردگی آزاد کی صورت میں ہم نے اس اصل کے خلاف اجماع صحابہ کی وجہ سے کیا ہے اور یہاں مکاتب و غلام میں یہ بات نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ ان کو آزاد کے ساتھ ملحق روایت ہے: ان امة اتت قوما فغرتهم وزحمت انها حرة فتزوجها رجل فولدت له اولاد افوجدها امة فقضى عمر بقيمة أولادها في كل مغرور غره حضرت عثمان سے بھی اسی طرح کی روایت ہے۔
Kitab al-Mukatab. Al-Ghurur (deception): And this is because he did not desire her marriage except to attain freedom of children. And for them (the two shaykhs) it is a child born between two slaves, so it is a slave. And this is because the original principle is that the child follows the mother in slavery and freedom. We have deviated from this principle in the case of a free man by consensus of the Companions. And this is not in its meaning because the right of the master there is compensated by a prompt price, and here by a deferred price until after emancipation, so it remains on the original principle and is not attached to him.
Translation: If a master marries his slave woman to his slave, then makes both mukatab, and the slave woman gives birth to a child, then this child will enter into the kitabah of the mother. And the earnings of the child will be for his mother. Because to be subordinate to the mother is stronger. That is why a child follows his mother in slavery and freedom. If a mukatab marries with the master's permission a woman who claimed to be free, and children are born, then the woman is proven to be a slave, then all her children will be owned and he cannot take them for a price. Similarly, the ruling for a slave whom the master permitted to marry. This is according to the two shaykhs. Imam Muhammad says that his children are free for a price. Because he has become a partner with the free man in the proof of this right, and that reason is deception. The reason is that the mukatab did not desire marriage to this woman except to obtain freedom of children. The proof of the two shaykhs is that this child is born among owned individuals, so it is also in bondage. And this is because the original principle is that a child follows his mother in slavery and freedom. In the case of a free man, we have acted contrary to this original principle due to the consensus of the Companions. And this is not in its meaning. Because there the master's right is compensated with a prompt price, and here it is compensated with a price that will be paid after freedom. So here the ruling will remain on the original principle and will not be attached to the mukatab. Explanation of his statement: 'And whoever marries his slave woman...' etc. If a master marries his slave woman to one of his slaves, then makes both mukatab, then a child is born, then the child will enter into the kitabah of the mother, and the earnings of this child will also go to the mother. Because the side of being subordinate to the mother is heavier. For this reason, a child follows his mother in freedom and slavery, i.e., if the mother is an owned woman, then the child will also be owned by her owner, even if the father is free. And if the mother is a free woman, then the child will also be free. If the child's father is a slave of someone, then in freedom and slavery the child follows his mother, and in lineage follows his father. His statement: 'And if the mukatab marries...' etc. If a mukatab or a ma'dhun slave marries with his master's permission a woman who claimed to be free, and children are born, later that woman turns out to be owned by someone, then the children will become owned by the owner of that woman. And according to the two shaykhs, the mukatab or ma'dhun slave cannot take the children by paying their price. According to Imam Muhammad, Imam Zufar, and the three Imams, he can take them by paying the price, meaning the children of the mukatab or slave will be free for a price. Benefit: Most of our companions have mentioned the statement of Imam Abu Yusuf with Imam Abu Hanifa, and Faqih Abu Layth has mentioned his statement with Imam Muhammad. But the correct is what the majority mentioned, because the final statement of Imam Abu Yusuf is this, as Imam Quduri clarified in Kitab al-Taqrib. His statement: 'Because he has become a partner of the free man...' etc. Imam Muhammad's proof is that the mukatab or ma'dhun slave is deceived, so his children become free with a price. Its explanation is that the mentioned right, i.e., the cause of the children becoming free for a price, the mukatab has become a partner with the free person in that cause, i.e., deception, because the mukatab only desired marriage to this woman to attain the honor of freedom of children. So just as a free man marries a woman under deception that she is free, then she turns out to be owned, and the children are freed for a price, similarly the children of the mukatab will also be free for a price, because he too has been deceived. So here the cause of freedom is only deception, and in this cause both the mukatab and the free man are equally partners. His statement: 'And for them it is a child...' etc. The proof of the two shaykhs is that that child is born between two slaves, i.e., the father is also owned (because as long as he is in kitabah, he is still a slave) and the mother is also owned (because due to proof of entitlement her slavery is manifest), so the child will also be owned. His statement: 'And this is because the original principle...' etc. That is, the ruling mentioned is because the established principle is that a child follows his mother in freedom and slavery. But in the case of a free man deceived, we have deviated from this principle due to the consensus of the Companions, and this does not apply here to the extent that they can be annexed to the free man. And leaving analogy due to the consensus of the Companions is because in the case of a free man, the right of the owner of the slave woman over these children is compensated by paying a prompt price, because a free man is the owner of everything, whereas the mukatab and slave are not owners of anything yet. And in the case of the mukatab and slave, in lieu of this right, only a price can be obtained that will be paid after they become free. So this is not similar to that. Therefore the ruling here remains according to the original analogy, i.e., the children will not be freed for a price. His statement: 'By consensus of the Companions...' etc. Allamah Ayni says that the claim of consensus of the Companions is open to consideration because there is established disagreement among the Companions regarding this. Thus Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated in al-Musannaf from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Regarding a man who bought a slave girl, and she bore children to him, then a man established a proof that she was his, he (Ali) said: She will be returned to him and her children will be assessed, and the seller will pay what he deceived.' And from Sulayman bin Yasar: 'That a slave woman came to a people and deceived them, claiming she was free, so a man married her, and she bore children to him, then he found she was a slave. So Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) decreed the value of her children in every case of a deceived person.' And from Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) a similar narration.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, an Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, discusses two related rulings concerning the offspring of a mukatab (a slave who has made a contract of manumission). The first ruling: if a master marries his slave woman to his male slave, then makes both mukatab, and the woman bears a child, that child enters into the mother's kitabah (contract), and the child's earnings go to the mother. The principle is that a child follows its mother in status of slavery or freedom. The second ruling: if a mukatab or a ma'dhun (permitted) slave marries a woman who falsely claims to be free (gharurah), and children are born, then according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) the children remain slaves and cannot be redeemed by paying their price. But Imam Muhammad and others hold that the children become free upon payment of their price. The passage then presents the proofs: Imam Muhammad argues that the mukatab is deceived (maghrur) just like a free man in similar circumstances, so by analogy (qiyas) the children should be freed for a price. The two shaykhs respond that the original principle is that a child follows its mother in slavery, and the exception for a free man is based on consensus of the Companions (ijma' as-sahabah) where the master's right is compensated by an immediate payment (qimah najizah). In the case of a mukatab or slave, payment can only be deferred until after emancipation, so the exception does not apply, and the original ruling that the child is a slave remains. The commentary also notes a difference of attribution regarding Abu Yusuf: most scholars align his final view with Abu Hanifa, while some align him with Muhammad. The correct position is that Abu Yusuf's final view is with Abu Hanifa. Additionally, Allamah Ayni questions the claim of consensus, citing reports from Ali, Umar, and Uthman that suggest disagreement among the Companions. The passage thus illustrates intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, application of qiyas, and the role of ijma' in overriding analogical reasoning.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract (kitabah) with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments over time. He remains a slave until the contract is fulfilled.
غرور (ghurur): Deception, where one party is misled by another's false claim (here, a woman claiming to be free). The deceived person (maghrur) may have rights to compensation or to have children freed.
شیخین (shaykhayn): Refers to the two primary authorities in the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Here, they hold the opposite view to Imam Muhammad on this issue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what is the status of children born to a mukatab who married a woman who falsely claimed to be free?
A) They become free immediately without payment.
B) They remain slaves and cannot be redeemed for a price.
C) They become free if the mukatab pays their price.
D) They are considered free because the father is a mukatab.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the exception for a deceived free man does not extend to a mukatab because the ‘illa is immediate payment, not deception alone.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
12 min
Offspring of a Mukatab Married Under Deception: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on children of a deceived mukatab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn on the status of children of a deceived mukatab, and explain the legal reasoning (qiyas vs. principle of following the mother) that leads to the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
The children of a deceived mukatab remain slaves because the exception for a free man cannot extend to a non-owner.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) over the legal consequences of a mukatab marrying a woman under deception about her free status. The ruling touches on the interplay between analogy (qiyas) based on a common cause ('illa) and the established principle that a child's status follows the mother. We will dissect each side's argument and conclude with the operative position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their positions
Recognize that Imam Muhammad argues for freeing the children with payment, while the Shaykhayn argue they remain slaves.
Imam Muhammad is al-Shaybani; Shaykhayn are Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (or Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in one riwaya).
2
Understand Imam Muhammad's analogy
Imam Muhammad extends the ruling of a free man deceived to a mukatab, claiming the same 'illa (deception) leads to the same right to free offspring.
The free man's offspring are freed with price based on ijma' of the Companions.
3
Analyze the Shaykhayn's counter-argument
The Shaykhayn assert that the child follows the mother in slavery, and the exception for the free man is based on his ability to pay cash immediately, which a mukatab lacks.
The principle is 'al-walad li al-firash' but here the mother is a slave; the exception is limited.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
The text indicates that the original analogy (qiyas) remains, so the children are not freed. The mufta bihi is the Shaykhayn's view.
The phrase 'لہذا یہاں حکم اصل قیاس کے موافق رہے گا' confirms this.
5
Note 'Ayni's critique of ijma'
Allamah 'Ayni questions the claim of ijma' by citing differences among the Companions, which weakens Imam Muhammad's proof.
This shows that claimed ijma' can be scrutinized.

قوله لا نه شارك الحر.. الخ - امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ مکاتب یا عبد ما زدن فریب خوردہ ہے تو اس کی اولاد قیمت کے ساتھ آزاد ہو جائے گی۔ اس کی تشریح یہ ہے کہ حق مذکور یعنی اولاد کے بقیمت آزاد ہونے کے ثابت ہونے کے سبب یعنی قریب میں وہ مکاتب آزاد شخص کا شریک ہو گیا۔ اس لئے کہ مکاتب نے اس عورت سے نکاح کی رغبت صرف اس لئے کی تھی کہ حریت اولاد کا شرف حاصل ہو تو جیسے کوئی آزاد آدمی کسی عورت کے آزاد ہونے کے دھوکے میں نکاح کر لے پھر وہ کسی کی مملوکہ نکلے تو اولا د قیمت آزاد ہوتی ہے اس طرح مکاتب کی اولاد بھی بقیمت آزاد ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس کو بھی دھوکا ہوا ہے۔ پس یہاں آزادی کا سبب فقط دھوکا ہے اور اس سبب میں مکاتب و آزاد دونوں یکساں شریک ہیں۔

قوله ولهما انه مولود... الخ ۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ اولا دور رقیقوں کے درمیان پیدا ہوئی ہے۔ یعنی باپ بھی مملوک ہے کیونکہ وہ جب تک کتابت میں ہے غلام ہی ہے ) اور ماں بھی مملوک ہے۔ (کیونکہ ثبوت استحقاق کی وجہ سے اس کی رقیت ظاہر ہو گئی ) تو اولاد بھی مملوک ہوگی۔ قوله وهذا لان الاصل .... الخ ۔ یعنی حکم مذکور اس لئے ہے کہ اصل یہی قرار پائی ہے کہ بچہ آزادی اور غلامی میں اپنی ماں کا تابع ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن فریب خوردگی آزاد کی صورت میں ہم نے اس اصل کے خلاف اجماع صحابہ کی وجہ سے کیا ہے اور یہاں مکاتب و غلام میں یہ بات نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ ان کو آزاد کے ساتھ ملحق کیا جا سکے۔ اور اجماع صحابہ کی وجہ سے ترک قیاس اس لئے ہے کہ آزاد کی صورت میں باندی کے آقا کا جوحق اس اولاد میں تھا وہ نقد قیمت دے کر پورا کر دیا جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ آزاد آدمی ہر چیز کا مالک ہوتا ہے اور مکاتب و غلام ابھی کسی چیز کا مالک نہیں ہے۔ اور مکاتب و غلام کی صورت میں اس حق کے عوض ایسی قیمت مل سکتی ہے جو ان کے آزاد ہو جانے کے بعد ادا ہوگی۔ پس یہ اس کے معنی میں ہوا۔ لہذا یہاں حکم اصل قیاس کے موافق رہے گا۔ یعنی اولا د قیمت آزاد نہ ہوگی۔ قوله باجماع الصحابة .... الخ - علامہ عینی فرماتے ہیں کہ اجماع صحابہ کا دعوی محل نظر ہے اس لئے کہ اس بارے میں صحابہ کرام .. کہ کا لوی نظر کہ میں کا اختلاف ثابت ہے۔ چنانچہ ابن ابی شیبہ نے مصنف میں حضرت علیؓ سے روایت کی ہے: في رجل اشترى جارية فولدت منه اولاد ائم اقام رجل البينة انهاله قال : ترد عليه وتقوم عليه ولدها فيغرم الذي باعها ما غرها

اسی طرح سلیمان بن بیار سے روایت ہے:

ان امة اتت قوما فغرتهم وزحمت انها حرة فتزوجها رجل فولدت له اولاد افوجدها امة فقضى عمر بقيمة أولادها في كل مغرور غره حضرت عثمان سے بھی اسی طرح کی روایت ہے۔
His statement: 'because he is a partner of the free man'... etc - Imam Muhammad's proof is that the mukatab or deceived slave, his offspring will be freed with price. Explanation: The mentioned right, i.e., the offspring being freed with price, the cause is that the mukatab became a partner of the free person. Because the mukatab desired marriage with this woman only to obtain the honor of free offspring. So just as a free man who marries a woman under deception that she is free, and then she is found to be owned by someone else, his offspring are freed with price, similarly the mukatab's offspring are freed with price because he too was deceived. So here the cause of freedom is only deception, and in this cause the mukatab and the free man are equal partners. His statement: 'and for them (the two) that he is born...' etc. The proof of the Shaykhayn is that the child is born between two slaves, i.e., the father is a slave (since as long as he is in kitabah he is a slave) and the mother is a slave (because due to the proof of entitlement her slavery became apparent), so the child is also a slave. His statement: 'and this is because the principle...' etc. That is, the mentioned ruling is because the established principle is that a child follows his mother in freedom and slavery. But in the case of a free man deceived, we have gone against this principle due to the consensus of the Companions, and here in the case of a mukatab and slave, this (going against principle) does not apply to the extent that they can be annexed to the free man. And the leaving of analogy due to the consensus of the Companions is because in the case of the free man, the right that the master of the slave woman had in her offspring is fulfilled by paying the price in cash, because a free man owns everything. But a mukatab and a slave do not yet own anything. And in the case of a mukatab and slave, in lieu of that right, only a price can be obtained that will be paid after they become free. So this is in its meaning. Therefore, here the ruling will be according to the original analogy, i.e., the offspring will not be freed with price. His statement: 'by consensus of the Companions'... etc. Allamah 'Ayni says that the claim of consensus of the Companions is open to scrutiny because there is proven disagreement among the Companions regarding this matter. Thus Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated in al-Musannaf from Hadrat Ali (RA): 'Regarding a man who bought a slave woman and she bore children from him, then a man establishes proof that she is his, he said: She is returned to him and her children are assessed as value against him, and the one who sold her must pay what he deceived.' Similarly, a narration from Sulayman ibn Yasar: 'A slave woman came to some people and deceived them, claiming she was free, so a man married her and she bore children for him. Then he found her to be a slave. So Umar (RA) judged the value of her children in every case of a deceived person.' A similar narration is from Hadrat Uthman (RA).
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the status of children born to a mukatab (a slave under a contract of manumission) who marries a woman under the false belief that she is free, but she is later revealed to be a slave owned by someone else. Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) argues that the children are freed upon paying their assessed value, analogizing this to the case of a free man who is similarly deceived. In that case, based on the consensus (ijma') of the Companions, the children are freed with compensation to the owner. Imam Muhammad sees the mukatab as sharing the same cause ('illa) of deception, thus the same ruling applies. The Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad's own teacher, Imam Abu Hanifa's view is represented here by the two) disagree. They argue that the child follows the mother in status of slavery because both parents are slaves at the time of birth (the father is still a slave during kitabah, and the mother's slavery is confirmed). The principle that a child follows the mother in freedom or slavery is well-established. The departure from this principle in the case of a free man is based on a specific ijma' of the Companions, which cannot be extended to a mukatab because a free man can pay the compensation immediately, whereas a mukatab cannot pay until after he becomes free. Therefore, the original analogy (qiyas) remains, and the children are not freed by payment. The commentator, Allamah 'Ayni, casts doubt on the claimed ijma' by citing narrations from Ali, Umar, and Uthman that suggest differing opinions among the Companions. However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Shaykhayn: the children remain slaves and are not freed with price.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered into a contract of kitabah with his master, whereby he will be freed upon paying a specified sum over a period.
غرور (ghurūr): Deception or fraud that leads a person to act under a false belief, here specifically regarding the status of a woman as free.
اجماع الصحابہ (ijmāʿ al-ṣaḥābah): Consensus of the Companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) claimed as a proof for the ruling on the free man's children in case of deception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the Shaykhayn give for not extending the free man's ruling to the mukatab?
A) The mukatab did not intend to marry a slave woman.
B) The mukatab cannot pay the compensation immediately, unlike the free man.
C) There is no ijma' regarding the mukatab.
D) The children follow the father, not the mother.

Key Takeaway
The children of a deceived mukatab are not freed with price; the mufta bihi is the Shaykhayn's view that they remain slaves due to the principle of following the mother and the mukatab's inability to pay immediately.

Nikah — Marriage

Uqr on a Mukatab for Intercourse with a Slave Woman
States the ruling on 'uqr for a mukatab's intercourse with a slave woman, distinguishing purchase and marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'uqr for a mukatab's intercourse with a slave woman, distinguish the timing based on purchase vs marriage, and apply the qiyas reasoning.

Core Idea
Uqr from trade is immediate in kitabah; from marriage deferred until freedom.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school on compensatory payment ('uqr) when a mukatab (a slave under a contract of manumission) has intercourse with a slave woman who later proves to be owned by another. The text distinguishes between two scenarios: if the intercourse occurred through a purchase (even invalid), the 'uqr is due immediately during kitabah; if through a marriage, it is deferred until freedom. The reasoning hinges on whether the act is within the scope of trade, which the kitabah contract covers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
State the ruling: A mukatab who has intercourse with a slave woman under a claim of purchase owes 'uqr, payable immediately in the kitabah. If under marriage, the 'uqr is not due until he becomes free.
2
Understand the qiyas structure
Identify the asl (purchase scenario) where 'uqr is immediate, and the far' (marriage scenario) where it is deferred. The illa (effective cause) is that purchase is a trade activity included under kitabah, while marriage is not.
Qiyas jali (clear analogy) because the illa is explicitly stated.
3
Apply to invalid purchase (fasid)
Even if the purchase is invalid (fasid), the 'uqr is still taken immediately because the transaction is still considered trade, which kitabah encompasses in both valid and invalid forms.
Analogous to an agent's actions: kitabah covers trade in all its types.
4
Examine the chain of necessity
Follow the reasoning: kitabah permits trade → purchase leads to dropping of hadd (due to shubha) → dropping hadd necessitates 'uqr → therefore kitabah necessitates 'uqr when the act is trade-related.
This chain explains why the 'uqr is tied to kitabah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وان وطى المكاتب امةً على وجه الملك بغير اذن المولى ثم استحقها رجل فعليه العقر يوخذ به في الكتابة وان وطيها على وجه النكاح لم يؤخذ به حتى يعتق و كذلك الماذون له ووجه الفرق ان في الفصل الاول ظهر الدين فى حق المولى لان التجارة وتوابعها داخلة تحت الكتابة وهذا العقر من توابعها لأنه لولا الشراء لما سقط الحد وما لم يسقط الحد لا يجب العقر اما لم يظهر فى الفصل الثاني لان النكاح ليس من الاكتساب في شيء فلا ينتظمه الكتابة كالكفالة. قال واذا اشترى المكاتب جارية شراء فاسدا ثم وطيها فردها أخذ بالعقر في المكاتبة وكذلك العبد المأذون له لانه من باب التجارة فان التصرف تارة يقع صحيحا ومرة يقع فاسدا والكتابة والاذن ينتظمانه بنوعيه كالتوكيل فكان ظاهرا في حق المولى

ترجمہ اگر ولی کی مکاتب نے کسی باندی سے ملک کے طور پر آقا کی اجازت کے بغیر پھر کوئی شخص اس کا مستحق نکل آیا تو مکاتب پر عقر واجب ہوگا جس کا مواخذہ - الت کتابت میں ہوگا اور اگر نکاح کے طور پر وطی کی تو عقر کا مواخذہ نہ ہوگا یہاں تک کہ وہ آزاد ہو جائے اور اس طرح عبد مازون ہے۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ پہلی صورت میں دین آقا کے حق میں ظاہر ہو گیا ۔ کیونکہ تجارت اور اس کے توابع کتابت کے تحت میں داخل ہیں اور یہ عقر توابع تجارت میں سے ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اگر خرید نہ ہوتی تو حد زناء ساقط نہ ہوتی اور جب تک حد ساقط نہ ہو عقر واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ لیکن دوسری صورت میں دین ظاہر نہیں ہوا کیونکہ نکاح اکتساب میں سے نہیں ہے تو کفالت کی طرح کتابت اس کو شامل نہ ہوگی ۔ اگر مکاتب نے شراء فاسد کے طور سے باندی خرید کر اس سے ولی کی پھر اس کو واپس کر دیا تو مقر کا مواخذہ حالت مکاتبت میں ہوگا۔ ایسے ہی عبد مازون ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ باب تجارت سے ہے اس لئے کہ تصرف کبھی صحیح اور کبھی فاسد واقع ہوتا ہے اور اذن وکتابت دونوں قسموں کو شامل ہے۔ جیسے وکیل کرنے میں ہے پس یہ آقا کے حق میں بھی ظاہر ہوگا۔ والحاصل ان الكتابة أوجبت الشراء والشراء اوجب سقوط الحد و سقوط الحداوجب العقر فالكتابة او جبت العقر
He (the author) said: If a mukatab has intercourse with a slave woman by way of ownership (i.e., purchase) without the master's permission, then a man claims her (as his property), then upon him is due the 'uqr, which is taken (from him) in the kitabah. And if he has intercourse with her by way of marriage, it is not taken (from him) until he becomes free. And similarly the one given permission (to trade). And the aspect of distinction is that in the first case, the debt (of 'uqr) becomes apparent in the right of the master because trade and its accessories are included under kitabah, and this 'uqr is from its accessories because had there been no purchase, the hadd (punishment for zina) would not have been dropped, and as long as the hadd is not dropped, the 'uqr is not obligatory. But in the second case, it does not become apparent because marriage is not from earning in any way, so kitabah does not encompass it, like kafalah (suretyship). He said: And if a mukatab buys a slave woman with a fasid (invalid) purchase, then has intercourse with her, then returns her, the 'uqr is taken from him in the kitabah. And similarly the slave given permission (to trade), because it is from the chapter of trade. For sometimes a transaction occurs validly and sometimes invalidly, and kitabah and permission encompass both types, like agency. So it becomes apparent in the right of the master. Translation: If a mukatab with a slave woman by way of ownership without the master's permission, then a person becomes entitled to her, then upon the mukatab is due 'uqr, which is taken in kitabah. And if he had intercourse by way of marriage, the 'uqr is not taken until he becomes free. Similarly the slave given permission. The aspect of distinction is that in the first case, the debt becomes apparent in the right of the master because trade and its accessories are included under kitabah, and this 'uqr is from its accessories, because if the purchase had not occurred, the hadd of zina would not have been dropped, and as long as hadd is not dropped, 'uqr is not obligatory. But in the second case, the debt does not become apparent because marriage is not from earning, so kitabah does not encompass it, like kafalah. If a mukatab buys a slave woman with a fasid purchase, then has intercourse, then returns her, the 'uqr is taken in kitabah. Similarly the slave given permission, because it is from the chapter of trade, for a transaction sometimes occurs validly and sometimes invalidly, and kitabah and permission encompass both types, like agency. So it becomes apparent in the right of the master. The summary: Kitabah necessitates purchase, purchase necessitates dropping of hadd, dropping of hadd necessitates 'uqr, so kitabah necessitates 'uqr.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and its legal reasoning (t'lil) concerning the 'uqr (compensatory dower) due from a mukatab (or a slave permitted to trade, 'abd ma'dhun) who has intercourse with a slave woman who turns out to be owned by someone else. The ruling distinguishes between two scenarios: (1) if the intercourse occurred through purchase (i.e., the mukatab bought the woman under the belief that she was his property, then had intercourse), the 'uqr is immediately enforceable during the period of kitabah because the debt arises from a trade-related transaction, which is included within the scope of the kitabah contract. (2) If the intercourse occurred through marriage (i.e., the mukatab married her under deception), the 'uqr is deferred until after he becomes free, because marriage is not a trade activity and thus is not covered by kitabah. The reason (wajh al-farq) is that the purchase is what caused the dropping of the hadd punishment for zina (since the act is not considered zina due to the mistaken claim of ownership), and the dropping of hadd necessitates the 'uqr. Therefore, the 'uqr is seen as a trade-related obligation. In contrast, marriage is not trade, and its obligations are not part of kitabah. The same principle applies to a fasid (invalid) purchase; even though the purchase is invalid, the 'uqr is still taken in kitabah because the act of trade (even if invalid) is within the scope of kitabah. The summary explains the chain: kitabah allows purchase; purchase leads to dropping of hadd; dropping of hadd necessitates 'uqr; thus kitabah indirectly necessitates 'uqr. This reasoning is based on qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).

Key Terms
عقر (ʿuqr): Compensatory dower paid by a man who has intercourse with a slave woman under a claim of right (such as purchase or marriage) when she is later found to belong to another. It is a financial obligation to compensate the owner for the use of the slave woman.
کتابت (kitābah): The contract of manumission by which a slave agrees to pay his master a specified sum over time, after which he becomes free. During the period, the slave retains some capacity for trade.
ماذون (maʾdhūn): A slave who has been given permission (idhn) by his master to engage in trade. He has similar limited capacity as a mukatab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the 'uqr for a mukatab's intercourse with a slave woman immediately taken in kitabah when done via purchase, but deferred when done via marriage?
A) Because purchase is a trade activity included under kitabah, while marriage is not.
B) Because the hadd punishment is not dropped in the case of marriage.
C) Because the master's permission is required for marriage but not for purchase.
D) Because the 'uqr for marriage is always higher.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school links the immediacy of 'uqr to whether the act falls within trade, which is the scope of the kitabah contract.

The Mukataba's Child: Choice Between Kitaba and Umm Walad
Explains options for a mukataba who bears a child from her master and consequences for the child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options available to a mukataba who bears her master's child and apply the rulings regarding lineage, freedom, and financial obligations.

Core Idea
A mukataba who bears her master's child may choose to continue the kitaba or become umm walad, with distinct consequences for her and her child.

This passage from Al-Hidayah deals with a unique scenario: a mukataba (a female slave under a kitaba contract) who bears a child from her master. The master's act of impregnation gives her two possible paths to freedom: immediate through the kitaba (but with financial obligation) or deferred without payment (by becoming umm walad). The ruling clarifies her right to choose and the subsequent effects on the child's status, inheritance, and financial liabilities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two choices
Note that the mukataba has a choice: continue the kitaba or declare herself incapable and become umm walad.
The choice is hers, not the master's.
2
Understand the reasoning
The passage explains that she now faces two directions of freedom: immediate with a price (kitaba) and deferred without price (umm walad).
This reasoning (talil) underlies the ruling.
3
Determine the child's status
The child's lineage is established from the master, and the child is free because the master can free him and his ownership suffices for istilad by claim.
The child becomes free regardless of the mother's choice.
4
Analyze financial consequences
If she continues the kitaba, she takes the 'aqr from the master. Upon his death, she becomes free by istilad and the kitaba debt falls. If she dies leaving property, the kitaba is paid from it and the remainder goes to her child as inheritance.
If she dies insolvent, no sa'aya is required from the child because he is free.
5
Examine the case of a second child
If she gives birth to another child not claimed by the master, that child is a dependent mukatab and must earn to pay the kitaba if she dies without fulfilling it. However, if the master dies later, that child becomes free and the sa'aya is nullified.
The master's claim determines the second child's status.

Source Text

فصل قال و اذا ولدت المكاتبة من المولى فهى بالخيار ان شاءت مضت على الكتابة وان شاءت عجزت نفسها وصارت ام ولد له لانها تلقتها جهتا حرية عاجلة ببدل وآجلة بغير بدل فتخير بينهما ونسب ولدها ثابت من المولى وهو حر لان المولى يملك الاعتاق فى ولدها وماله من الملك يكفى لصحة الاستيلاد بالدعوة واذا مضت على الكتابة اخذت العقر من مولاها لاختصاصها بنفسها وبمنافعها على ما قدمنا ثم ان مات المولى عتقت بالاستيلاد وسقط عنها بدل الكتابة وان ماتت هى وتركت مالا تودى منه مكاتبتها وما بقى ميراث لابنها جريا على موجب الكتابة فان لم تترك مالا فلا سعاية على الولد لانه حر ولو ولدت ولدا آخر لم يلزم المولى الا ان يدعى لحرمة وطيها عليه فلو لم يدع وماتت من غير وفاء يسعى هذا الولد لانه مکاتب تبعًا لها فلومات المولى بعد ذلك عتق وبطل عنه السعاية لانه بمنزلة ام الولد اذهو ولدها فيتبعها
ترجمہ ( فصل ) اگر مکاتبہ نے بچہ جنا آقا سے تو اس کو اختیار ہے چاہے کتابت پوری کرے چاہے خود کو عاجز کر کے اس کی ام ولد ہو جائے ۔ کیونکہ اس کو آزادی کی دو جہتیں حاصل ہو گئیں۔ ایک بدل کے ذریعہ فی الفور آزادی اور ایک بلا بدل مؤخر آزادی۔ پس وہ دونوں میں مختار ہوگی۔ اور اس کے بچہ کا نسب آقا سے ثابت ہو گا اور وہ آزاد ہو گا۔ کیونکہ آقا اس کے بچہ کو آزاد کر سکتا ہے اور آقا کی جو ملک ہے وہ دعوی استیلاد کی صحت کے لئے کافی ہے۔ اب اگر مکاتبہ نے کتابت پوری کی تو آقا سے اپنا عقر لے لے۔ کیونکہ اس کو اپنی ذات اور منافع کا اختصاص حاصل ہے۔ جیسا کہ ہم پہلے ذکر کر چکے۔ پھر اگر آقا مر جائے تو وہ ام ولد ہونے کی وجہ سے آزاد ہو جائے گی۔ اور عوض اس کے ذمہ سے ساقط ہو جائیگا۔ اور اگر وہ خود مرگئی اور کچھ مال چھوڑ گئی تو اس سے بدل کتابت ادا کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور جو باقی رہے وہ اس کے بیٹے کے لئے میراث
Section: He said: When the mukataba (female mukatab) gives birth to a child from the master, she has a choice: if she wishes, she continues on the kitaba, and if she wishes, she declares herself incapable and becomes his umm walad. This is because she has encountered two directions of freedom: one immediate with a price, and one deferred without a price, so she chooses between them. The lineage of her child is established from the master, and he is free, because the master has the power to free her child, and his ownership is sufficient for the validity of istilad by claim. If she continues on the kitaba, she takes the 'aqr from her master due to her exclusive right to herself and her benefits, as we have previously mentioned. Then, if the master dies, she becomes free by istilad and the price of the kitaba falls from her. If she dies and leaves property, her kitaba is paid from it, and what remains is inheritance for her son, consistent with the requirement of the kitaba. If she leaves no property, then there is no earning (sa'aya) on the child because he is free. If she gives birth to another child, it is not binding on the master unless he claims it, due to the prohibition of intercourse with her. If he does not claim it and she dies without fulfilling the kitaba, this child must earn (sa'aya) because he is a mukatab dependent on her. If the master dies after that, he becomes free and the sa'aya is nullified, because he is like the child of an umm walad, following her. Translation: Section: If the mukataba gave birth to a child from the master, she has the choice: either she fulfills the kitaba, or she declares herself incapable and becomes his umm walad. This is because two avenues of freedom have come to her: one immediate through payment, and one deferred without payment. So she may choose between them. The lineage of her child is established from the master, and he is free, because the master can free the child, and his ownership is sufficient for the validity of the claim of istilad. If she fulfills the kitaba, she takes her 'aqr from the master, because she has exclusive right to herself and her benefits, as we mentioned before. Then, if the master dies, she becomes free due to being umm walad, and the kitaba payment falls from her. If she herself dies and leaves some property, the kitaba payment is made from it, and what remains is inheritance for her son.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary of Al-Hidayah, addressing the situation of a mukataba (a female slave under a kitaba contract) who bears a child from her master. She is given a choice: either to continue with her kitaba (paying installments to become free) or to declare herself incapable (tajiz) and become umm walad (mother of the master's child). The reason is that she now has two possible paths to freedom: one through the kitaba (immediate but with payment) and one through istilad (deferred, upon the master's death, without payment). She may choose the one she prefers. If she chooses to continue the kitaba, she is entitled to take the 'aqr (compensation) from the master for the intercourse, because she owns her own self and her benefits (unlike an ordinary slave). If the master dies, she becomes free by istilad and the kitaba debt is cancelled. If she dies leaving property, the kitaba is paid from her estate, and the remainder is inherited by her child (who is free). If she leaves no property, there is no sa'aya (earning obligation) on the child because he is free. If she gives birth to another child (not claimed by the master), that child is not attributed to the master unless he claims it. If he does not claim it and she dies without fulfilling the kitaba, this child must earn (sa'aya) to pay off the kitaba, because he is a dependent mukatab (following her status). However, if the master dies after that, the child becomes free and the sa'aya is void, because he is in the status of a child of an umm walad, following his mother.

Key Terms
المكاتبة (al-mukataba): A female slave who has entered into a kitaba contract with the master.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bears a child from her master; upon the master's death, she becomes free.
السعاية (al-sa'ayah): Earnings or work required from a mukatab or dependent to fulfill the kitaba.
الاستيلاد (al-istilad): The act of a master impregnating his female slave, resulting in the child's freedom and the mother's status as umm walad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) She does not get any 'aqr
B) She takes the 'aqr from the master immediately
C) She must wait until she is free to take the 'aqr
D) The child takes the 'aqr

Key Takeaway
A mukataba who bears her master's child has the right to choose between continuing the kitaba or becoming umm walad, with specific rules for the child's freedom and financial obligations.

Kitabah by a Marid: Applying the One-Third Rule to Deferment
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kitabah by marid: Sahibayn vs Muhammad on one-third calculation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the views of the Sahibayn and Imam Muhammad regarding the application of the one-third rule to a kitabah contract made by a terminally ill master, and calculate the immediate payment required from the mukatab in each case.

Core Idea
In kitabah by a marid, the Sahibayn apply one-third to the entire price; Muhammad to the slave's value only.

This lesson examines a classical intra-Hanafi dispute about how the one-third rule affects a kitabah contract made by a terminally ill master. The passage from Al-Hidayah presents the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf against that of Imam Muhammad, focusing on whether the deferment is treated as part of the donation. Understanding this difference is crucial for calculating the mukatab's obligations when heirs do not permit the deferment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the dispute
Read the case: a marid master makes his slave (value 1000) a mukatab for 2000 payable in one year, dies with no other assets, and heirs do not permit the deferment. Note that there is an excess (muhabah) of 1000.
The one-third rule restricts donations (tabarru') to one-third of the estate.
2
State the Sahibayn's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the mukatab must pay two-thirds of the entire named price (2000) immediately, i.e., 1333.33, and the rest at the term, or be enslaved. Their reasoning: the whole price is badal al-raqabah, and the heirs' right to the slave extends to the price. The deferment is a relinquishment (isqat) of the right to immediate payment, so it is a donation from the one-third of the total.
They analogize to a sale of property by a marid.
3
State Imam Muhammad's position and reasoning
Imam Muhammad holds that the mukatab pays two-thirds of the slave's value (1000) immediately, i.e., 666.67, and the rest at the term. His reasoning: the master could have made kitabah at value without excess, so the excess is a gift. The deferment is also a gift. Both are donations from the one-third of the value, not the total price.
He analogizes to khul' divorce by a marid.
4
Examine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
The immediate payment differs by 666.66. Under the Sahibayn, the mukatab pays more upfront; under Muhammad, he pays less. The difference reflects whether the deferment is considered a donation from the entire price or only from the value.
The Sahibayn's view is generally the mufta bihi (operative for fatwa).
5
Apply to the second scenario (muhabah in both price and deferment)
When the kitabah price is less than the slave's value (price 1000, value 2000), there is muhabah in both the price (underpayment) and the deferment. All imams agree: the mukatab pays two-thirds of the value (1333.33) immediately or is enslaved. Here the one-third is calculated on the value, as the donor could have given the excess as a gift.
This shows consensus when muhabah is in both aspects.

قال و اذا كاتب المريض عبده على الفي درهم الى سنة وقيمته الف ثم مات ولا مال له غيره ولم يجز الورثة فانه يؤدى ثلثى الالفين حالا والباقى الى اجله او يرد رقيقا عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف وعند محمد يؤدى ثلثى الألف حالا والباقى الى اجله لان له ان يترك الزيادة بان يكاتيه على قيمته فله ان يؤخرها فصار كما اذا خالع المريض امرأته على الف الى سنة جاز لان له ان يطلقها بغير بدل لهما ان جميع المسمى بدل الرقبة حتى أجرى عليها احكام الابدال وحق الورثة متعلق بالمبدل فكذا بالبدل والتاجيل اسقاط معنى فيعتبر من ثلث الجميع بخلاف الخلع لان البدل فيه لا يقابل المال فلم يتعلق حق الورثة بالمبدل فلا يتعلق بالبدل ونظير هذا اذا باع المريض داره بثلاثة آلاف الى سنة وقيمتها الف ثم مات ولم يُجز الورثة فعندهما يقال للمشترى اذ ثلثى جميع الثمن حالا والثلث الى اجله والا فانقض البيع وعنده يعتبر الثلث بقدر القيمة لا فيما زاد عليه لما بينا من المعنى. قال وان كاتبه على الف سنة وقيمته الفان ولم يُجز الورثة يقال له ات ثلثى القيمة حالا او ترد رقيقا في قولهم جميعا لان المحاباة ههنا في القدر والتاخير فاعتبر الثلث فيهما
ترجمہ اگر مکاتب کیا مریض نے اپنے غلام کو دو ہزار درہم پر ایک سال کی میعاد تک اور غلام کی قیمت ایک ہزار ہے پھر مریض مر گیا اور اس غلام کے علاوہ کچھ مال نہیں ہے اور ورثہ نے میعاد کی اجازت نہیں دی تو مکاتب دو ہزار کی دو تہائی فی الحال اور باقی میعاد تک ادا کرے یا اس کو رقیق کر دیا جائیگا۔ شیخین کے نزدیک اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ایک ہزار کی دو تہائی فی الحال اور باقی میعاد تک ادا کرے گا۔ کیونکہ مریض کو یہ اختیار تھا کہ زیادتی ترک کر دے بایں طور کہ صرف اس کی قیمت پر مکاتب کرے تو وہ زیادتی کو مؤخر بھی کر سکتا ہے اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے مریض نے اپنی بیوی کو ایک ہزار پر ایک سال کی میعاد سے ضلع دیا تو یہ جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کو بلاعوض طلاق دینے کا اختیار ہے۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جمیع مسمی رقبہ کا بدل ہے ۔ حتی کہ پورے مسمی پر عوضوں کے احکام جاری کئے گئے ہیں اور ورثہ کا حق مبدل سے متعلق ہے تو ایسے ہی اس کے بدل سے بھی متعلق ہوگا اور میعاد دینا معنی استقاط حق ہے تو اس کا اعتبار کل کی تہائی سے ہو گا۔ بخلاف ضلع کے کہ اس میں عوض مال کے مقابلہ میں نہیں ہے تو ورثہ کا حق مبدل سے متعلق نہ ہوا۔ پس بدل نے بھی متعلق نہ ہو گا اور اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ مریض نے اپنا گھر تین ہزار کے عوض ایک سال کی میعاد سے فروخت کیا اور گھر کی قیمت ایک ہزار ہے پھر وہ مر گیا اور ورثہ نے میعاد کی اجازت نہیں دی تو شیخین کے نزدیک مشتری سے کہا جائے گا کہ پورے شمن کی دو تہائی فی الحال اور ایک تہائی میعاد پر ادا کر ور نہ بیچ توڑ دے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک صرف مقدار قیمت کی تہائی معتبر ہوگی نہ کہ اس سے زیادہ کی اسی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی۔ اور اگر مکاتب کیا اس کو ایک ہزار پر ایک سال کی میعاد سے اور اس کی قیمت دو ہزار ہے اور ورثہ نے اجازت نہیں دی تو مکاتب سے کہا جائے گا کہ اپنی دو تہائی قیمت فی الحال ادا کر ورنہ رقیق کر دیا جائے گا۔ سب کے قول میں کیونکہ یہاں محاباة مقدار اور میعاد
He said: When a sick man (marid) makes his slave a mukatab for two thousand dirhams for one year, and the slave's value is one thousand, then he dies and has no other property, and the heirs do not permit [the deferment], then he (the mukatab) shall pay two-thirds of the two thousand immediately and the rest at its term, or he shall be returned to slavery according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, he shall pay two-thirds of the one thousand immediately and the rest at its term, because the sick man could have left out the excess by making him a mukatab at his value, so he can also postpone it. Thus it becomes like when a sick man divorces his wife by khul' for one thousand for one year, it is valid because he could divorce her without compensation. [The two elders (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that] all the named amount is the price of the slave's person, such that the rules of exchanges are applied to it, and the right of the heirs is attached to the thing exchanged (mubdal), so similarly to the exchange (badal). And the deferment is a relinquishment of a right, so it is considered from one-third of the total. Unlike khul', because the compensation therein does not correspond to property, so the heirs' right is not attached to the mubdal, thus not to the badal. The analogy of this is: if a sick man sells his house for three thousand to a term of one year, and its value is one thousand, then he dies and the heirs do not permit, then according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the buyer is told: pay two-thirds of the entire price immediately and one-third at its term, otherwise the sale is rescinded. According to Muhammad, the one-third is considered according to the value, not on what exceeds it, for the reason we stated. He said: And if he made him a mukatab for one thousand for one year, and his value is two thousand, and the heirs do not permit, then he is told: bring two-thirds of the value immediately, or be returned to slavery, according to all of them, because the favoritism (muhabah) here is in the amount and the deferment, so the one-third is considered in both. Translation: If a sick man made his slave a mukatab for two thousand dirhams for one year, and the slave's value is one thousand, then he died and has no other property, and the heirs did not permit the deferment, then the mukatab shall pay two-thirds of two thousand immediately and the remainder at its term, or he shall be made a slave again. According to the two elders (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and according to Imam Muhammad, he shall pay two-thirds of one thousand immediately and the remainder at its term. Because the sick man had the option to leave out the excess by making him a mukatab at his value only, so he can also postpone it. And this is like when a sick man divorces his wife by khul' for one thousand with a one-year term, it is valid, because he has the option to divorce without compensation. The evidence of the two elders is that all the named amount is the price of the slave's person, such that the rules of exchanges are applied to the entire named amount, and the right of the heirs is attached to the thing exchanged (mubdal), so similarly to the exchange (badal). And granting the term is a relinquishment of a right, so it is considered from one-third of the total. Unlike khul', because the compensation therein does not correspond to property, so the heirs' right is not attached to the mubdal, thus not to the badal. Its analogy is: if a sick man sold his house for three thousand for a one-year term, and its value is one thousand, then he died and the heirs did not permit, then according to the two elders, the buyer is told: pay two-thirds of the entire price immediately and one-third at its term, otherwise rescind the sale. According to Imam Muhammad, only one-third of the value is considered, not on what exceeds it, for the reason we stated. And if he made him a mukatab for one thousand for one year, and his value is two thousand, and the heirs did not permit, then the mukatab is told: bring two-thirds of the value immediately, or be returned to slavery, according to all of them, because here the favoritism is in the amount and the deferment, so the one-third is considered in both.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of a kitabah contract made by a terminally ill master (marid) when the heirs do not permit the deferment. The case: the master makes his slave (worth 1000) a mukatab for 2000 payable in one year, then dies leaving only this slave. The heirs do not permit the deferment. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (Sahibayn), the slave must pay two-thirds of the entire 2000 immediately and the remainder at its term, or else be returned to slavery. According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, he pays two-thirds of the value (i.e., of 1000) immediately and the rest at its term. The reasoning: the entire named amount (2000) is considered the price of the slave's person (badal al-raqabah). The heirs' right is in the slave himself (mubdal), so it extends to the price. The deferment is a relinquishment of the right to immediate payment, so it is a form of gift (tabarru') from the master's one-third. The Sahibayn treat the deferment as affecting the entire price, so the one-third is calculated on the total. Muhammad argues that the master could have made the kitabah at the slave's value (1000) without excess, so the excess is a gift; the master could also postpone, so the deferment is also a gift; thus the one-third applies to the value, not the excess. The passage draws an analogy to khul' divorce and sale of property by a marid. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn, as indicated in the commentary. A second scenario: if the slave is worth 2000 and the kitabah is for 1000, then the favoritism (muhabah) is in the price and deferment; all agree the slave pays two-thirds of the value (i.e., 1333.33) immediately or be returned to slavery.

Key Terms
مريض (marid): A terminally ill person whose transactions are subject to the one-third rule for bequests.
محاباة (muhabah): Favoritism; giving more than fair value in a transaction; here it refers to the excess of the kitabah amount over the slave's value.
ثلث (thulth): The one-third of the estate that a marid can dispose of freely for donations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a marid master who makes a slave worth 1,000 a mukatab for 2,000 payable in one year, leaving no other property, and heirs do not permit, what does Imam Muhammad say the mukatab must pay immediately?
A) 1,333 dirhams (two-thirds of 2,000)
B) 667 dirhams (two-thirds of 1,000)
C) 1,000 dirhams (full value)
D) 2,000 dirhams (full price)

Key Takeaway
In a kitabah by a terminally ill master, the Sahibayn require the mukatab to pay two-thirds of the entire price immediately, while Muhammad requires two-thirds of the slave's value only, due to differing treatments of deferment as a donation.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Free Person's Kitabah on Behalf of a Slave: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Ruling on free person contracting kitabah for a slave with and without condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on a free person's kitabah for an absent slave, identify the role of istihsan, and contrast it with the qiyas-based view of the opposing schools.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas: a free person's payment frees the slave even without explicit condition, because no harm befalls the absent slave.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario where a free person initiates a kitabah contract on behalf of an absent slave. The Hanafi school employs istihsan to validate the contract and grant freedom upon payment, diverging from the strict qiyas that would deny freedom. Understanding this dispute highlights the flexibility of Hanafi methodology in seeking equitable outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Distinguish between the case where the free man includes an explicit condition linking payment to freedom and the case where he does not. Note the master's acceptance in both.
The condition is 'on condition that if I pay you, he is free'.
2
Apply qiyas to the scenario without condition
By qiyas, the slave is not freed because the contract lacks a condition and is suspended (mawquf). The three Imams uphold this view.
Qiyas here is strict analogy to other suspended contracts.
3
Introduce istihsan as Hanafi preference
The Hanafi school adopts istihsan: the slave is freed because there is no harm to the absent slave in making freedom conditional on the free man's payment. The contract is valid regarding freedom.
Istihsan is a key Hanafi source that allows departure from qiyas for equity.
4
Contrast with opposing schools' view
The opposing schools (a'imma thalatha) argue that the free man has no authority (wilayah) over the absent slave, so the contract is void (batil) regardless of condition. They rely on qiyas and reject istihsan.
This disagreement is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Articulate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Hanafi law, the slave becomes free upon payment; under the opposing view, the slave remains a slave and the payment is ineffective.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is the Hanafi istihsan.

قال واذا كاتب الحر عن عبد بالف درهم فان ادى عنه عتق وان بلغ العبد فقبل فهو مكاتب وصورة المسألة ان يقول الحر لمولى العبد كاتب عبدك على الف درهم على انى ان اديت اليک الفا فهو حر فكاتبه المولى على هذا فيعتق بادائه بحكم الشرط واذا قبل العبد صار مكاتبا لان الكتابة كانت موقوفة على اجازته وقبوله اجازة ولو لم يقل على انى ان اديت اليک الفا فهو حر فادى لا يعتق قياسا لانه لا شرط والعقد موقوف وفى الاستحسان يعتق لانه لا ضرر للعبد الغائب فى تعليق العتق باداء القائل فيصح في حق هذا الحكم ويتوقف في حق لزوم الالف على العبد وقيل هذه هى صورة مسألة الكتاب ولو ادى الحر البدل لا يرجع على العبد لانه متبوع ترجمہ اگر کسی آزاد شخص نے غلام کی طرف سے ہزار درہم پر کتابت ٹھہرائی۔ پس اگر اس کی طرف سے ادا کر دیا تو وہ آزاد ہو گیا اور اگر غلام کوخبر پہنچی اور اس نے قبول کر لیا تو وہ مکاتب ہے۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ آزاد شخص غلام کے آقا سے یہ کہے کہ اپنے غلام کو ایک ہزار کے عوض مکاتب کر اس شرط پر کہ اگر میں تجھ کو ہزار دے دوں تو وہ آزاد ہے۔ آقا نے اس کو اس قرار پر مکاتب کر دیا تو وہ اس کے ادا کرنے سے بحکم شرط آزاد ہو جائیگا۔ اور اگر غلام نے قبول کر لیا تو مکاتب ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ کتابت اس کی اجازت پر موقوف تھی اور اس کا قبول کرنا اجازت ہے اور اگر اس شخص نے یہ نہ کہا ہو ان ادیت الیک الفا فھو پھر اس نے ادا کر دیا تو قیا ساوہ آزاد نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کوئی شرط نہیں ہے اور عقد موقوف ہے اور استحسانا آزاد ہو جائیگا۔ کیونکہ قائل کے ادا کرنے پر آزادی کے متعلق ہونے میں غائب غلام کا کوئی ضرر نہیں ۔ پس اس حکم میں صحیح ہوگا۔ اور غلام پر ہزار لازم ہونے کے حق میں موقوف ہوگا۔ اور بقول بعض مسئلہ کتاب کی صورت بھی یہی ہے۔ اور اگر آزاد شخص نے عوض ادا کر دیا تو وہ غلام سے واپس نہیں لے سکتا۔ کیونکہ وہ احسان کنندہ ہے۔ تشریح قوله باب الخ - اس سے اس بات کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ صورت مسئلہ کی بابت شراح جامع صغیر کا اختلاف ہے. چنانچہ بعض شراح نے وہ صورت ذکر کی ہے جو صاحب ہدایہ نے مسئلہ کے آغاز میں دو صورة المسالۃ الھ سے ذکر کی ہے۔ اور بعض نے یہ صورت بیان کی ہے جو موصوف نے ولو لم يقل اٹھ سے ذکر کی ہے۔
If a free person makes a kitabah on behalf of a slave for one thousand dirhams, and he pays on his behalf, the slave is freed. If the slave learns and accepts, he becomes a mukatab. The scenario: the free man says to the master, 'Make kitabah for your slave for one thousand dirhams on condition that if I pay you one thousand, he is free.' The master does so. By payment, the slave is freed by virtue of the condition. If the slave accepts, he becomes mukatab because the kitabah was suspended on his permission, and his acceptance is permission. If he did not say 'on condition that if I pay you one thousand, he is free' and paid, by qiyas he is not freed because there is no condition and the contract is suspended. By istihsan he is freed because there is no harm to the absent slave in suspending freedom on the payment; so it is valid regarding this ruling and suspended regarding the obligation of the one thousand on the slave. It is said this is the scenario of the book. If the free man pays the compensation, he cannot take it back from the slave because he is a benefactor.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage discusses the situation where a free person (ajnabi) initiates a kitabah contract on behalf of a slave. The ruling is presented in two forms: one with an explicit condition that payment by the free man frees the slave, and one without such a condition. In the first form, if the free man says 'on condition that if I pay you, he is free,' then payment frees the slave immediately by virtue of the condition. The absent slave's acceptance is required for the contract to become binding on him; if he accepts, he becomes a mukatab. In the second form, without the condition, qiyas (analogy) would hold that the slave is not freed because the contract lacks a condition and is suspended. However, the Hanafi school adopts istihsan (juridical preference) and rules that the slave is freed because there is no harm to the absent slave in making his freedom conditional on the free man's payment; the contract is valid regarding freedom but suspended regarding the financial obligation on the slave. The passage also notes a difference of opinion among commentators of al-Jami' al-Saghir regarding the precise scenario. The free man cannot recover the payment from the slave because he acted voluntarily.

Key Terms
كتابة (kitabah): A contract by which a slave purchases his freedom by paying a specified amount in installments.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract and is in the process of paying for his freedom.
استحسان (istihsan): Juridical preference that deviates from strict analogy (qiyas) for a more equitable outcome.
فضولي (fuduli): A person who acts without authorization but on behalf of another, whose actions are suspended on the principal's ratification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a free person makes kitabah on behalf of a slave without an explicit condition (i.e., without saying 'on condition that if I pay, he is free'), what is the Hanafi ruling on the slave's freedom if the free person pays the amount?
A) The slave is not freed, neither by qiyas nor by istihsan.
B) By qiyas the slave is not freed, but by istihsan he is freed.
C) The slave is freed by qiyas because payment constitutes a valid condition.
D) The slave is freed only if the absent slave later accepts the contract.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a free person to free a slave via kitabah through istihsan, even without an explicit condition, prioritizing harm prevention over strict analogy.

Joint Kitaba: Liability of the Absent Slave
Explains why the master cannot demand kitaba payment from an absent slave in a joint kitaba contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding the master's right to demand payment from an absent slave in a joint kitaba contract and explain the reasoning using the analogy with kafala.

Core Idea
The absent slave is not liable because he is merely a follower; his acceptance does not change the contract.

This passage is a commentary on a line from Al-Hidayah that addresses a joint kitaba contract involving two slaves, one present and one absent. The commentator clarifies why the master has no right to demand the kitaba payment from the absent slave, even if the absent slave later accepts the contract. The reasoning is based on the principle that the absent slave is included only as a follower (taba'an) and his acceptance or rejection has no effect on the existing contract. The text provides a powerful analogy with kafala (guarantee) to solidify this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
Recognize that this is a joint kitaba (contract for gradual emancipation) where one slave is present at the time of contract and another is absent. The question is: can the master demand the payment from the absent slave?
2
State the ruling
The master has no right to demand the kitaba payment from the absent slave. The contract is valid only on the liability of the present slave.
3
Understand the reason
The absent slave is included only as a follower (taba'an). No payment has been placed on his liability. The contract is already executed on the present slave's liability alone.
4
Analyze the effect of acceptance
Whether the absent slave accepts the contract or rejects it, the ruling does not change. Acceptance does not create liability; rejection does not relieve the present slave.
5
Trace the qiyas (analogy)
The ruling is supported by an analogy to a guarantee (kafala) given without the debtor's permission. If the debtor later approves, the guarantor cannot recover the payment from the debtor because the act was voluntary. Similarly, the absent slave's acceptance does not make him liable because the kitaba was concluded by the present slave alone.
This qiyas is jaliy (clear) because the illa (effective cause) is the absence of direct obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وليس للمولى ... الخ - اور آقا کو غائب سے بدل کتابت کے مطالبہ کا کچھ اختیار نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ وہ حاضر کی کتابت میں تبعا داخل ہے اور اس کے ذمہ کچھ عوض نہیں ہے۔ پھر غائب غلام عقد کتابت قبول کرے یا نہ کرے اس سے کچھ تغیر نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ عقد کتابت حاضر غلام کے ذمہ باقی رہے گا۔ کیونکہ کتابت تو اس کے ذمہ قبول غائب کے بغیر ہی نافذ ہو چکی تو غائب کا قبول کرنا یا رد کرنا کچھ مؤثر نہ ہوگا۔ اس کی نظیر ایسی ہے جیسے کسی نے دوسرے کی طرف سے اس کے حکم کے بغیر کفالت کر لی۔ پھر مغول عنہ کواس کی خبر پہنچی اور اس نے کفالت کو جائز رکھا تو حکم متغیرنہیں ہوتا بلکہ فیل متبرع ہی باقی رہتا ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر کفیل نے مال کفالت ادا کر دیا تو وہ مکفول عنہ سے واپس نہیں لے سکتا پس جیسے مکفول عنہ کے قبول کرنے سے کفالت میں ایسا تغیر نہیں ہوتا کہ کفیل کو واپس لینے کا اختیار حاصل ہو ۔ ایسے ہی غائب غلام کے قبول کرنے سے کفالت سے وہ مال کا ذمہ دارنہ ہو جائے گا۔
His statement: 'And the master does not have...' - The master has no right to demand the kitaba payment from the absent slave. Because he (the absent slave) is included as a follower in the kitaba of the present slave, and there is no consideration on his liability. Then whether the absent slave accepts the kitaba contract or not, it will not change anything. Rather, the kitaba contract will remain on the liability of the present slave, because the kitaba has already been executed on his liability without the acceptance of the absent one. So the absent slave's acceptance or rejection has no effect. Its example is like someone becoming a guarantor on behalf of another without his permission. Then the guaranteed person hears about it and approves of the guarantee, the ruling does not change; rather, the voluntary act remains as it is. Even if the guarantor pays the guarantee amount, he cannot take it back from the guaranteed person. Just as the acceptance of the guaranteed person does not bring about such a change in the guarantee that the guarantor gets the right to take it back, similarly, the acceptance of the absent slave does not make him liable for the payment.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line from Al-Hidayah regarding a joint kitaba contract where one slave is present (has entered the contract) and another is absent. The commentator clarifies that the master has no right to demand the kitaba payment from the absent slave. The reason is that the absent slave is merely a follower (taba'an) in the kitaba of the present slave, and no payment is on his liability. The contract is concluded only on the present slave's liability. The acceptance or rejection by the absent slave does not change the contract. The commentator provides an analogy with a guarantee (kafala): if someone voluntarily guarantees another's debt without the debtor's permission, and later the debtor approves, the guarantor cannot recover the payment from the debtor. Similarly, the absent slave's acceptance does not make him liable. This ruling is from the Hanafi school and is based on the principle that the absent slave is not a direct party to the kitaba contract.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitaba contract with his master, agreeing to pay a sum for his freedom in installments.
بدل کتابت (badal al-kitaba): The payment (price) agreed upon in the kitaba contract for the slave's freedom.
كفالت (kafala): A contract of guarantee where one person becomes surety for another's debt or presence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a joint kitaba with one present and one absent slave, who is liable for the kitaba payment according to the Hanafi school?
A) Both slaves are equally liable.
B) Only the present slave is liable.
C) Only the absent slave is liable after he accepts.
D) No one is liable until both accept.

Key Takeaway
The absent slave is not liable for kitaba payment because he is not a direct party; his acceptance does not change his liability.
